No cancellation concern (bounded pure computation); errors propagate as a ConvertError Result up through the binder into the unified startup-diagnostics chain. Because it is pure and Send, it composes with structured-concurrency background-bootstrap of slow beans without context hazards.

#### Runtime ConversionService registry (Spring-faithful) — TypeId-keyed converter table
Mirror Spring directly: a `ConversionService` is a leaf bean holding a registry keyed by (source TypeId, target TypeId) -> boxed converter. `trait Converter: Send + Sync { fn convert(&self, raw: &ConfigValue, target: TargetHint, ctx: &ConvertCtx) -> Result<ErasedValue, ConvertError>; }` where ErasedValue is `Box<dyn Any + Send + Sync>` (or an Arc thereof). The container builds a DefaultConversionService at refresh, populates it with built-in converters (number/bool/enum/Duration/DataSize/Period/collection), then lets user converter beans register (the @ConfigurationPropertiesBinding analogue: a `#[converter]` attribute marks a bean contributed into the conversion registry early, before other post-processors). Lookup does a graph search: exact (src,tgt) hit, else try registered GenericConverter predicates, else error listing tried converters. The binder/@Value path calls `conversion_service.convert::<T>(raw, ctx)` which erases to TypeId, looks up, converts, downcasts back to T. Collection/enum converters are registered entries, not trait impls, so they are introspectable and replaceable wholesale at runtime.

**Pros:** Highest intent-parity with Spring (invariant 2 says intent not mechanism, but this gives the familiar 'central, pluggable, introspectable ConversionService' mental model and DX for Spring migrants); Fully dynamic: supports arbitrary (src,tgt) conversions, GenericConverter-style predicate converters, and converting between two runtime-erased types — the general case the trait approach cannot express; A user can enumerate, inspect, override, or replace the whole service (one bean), matching Spring's 'register a converter bean' exactly; great for an autowiring path that needs to coerce without static target type; Converter registration is origin-agnostic: a converter is a dyn trait object, so a WASM-module-supplied converter could register identically (honors the origin-agnostic guardrail); Diagnostics can introspect the registry to list 'converters considered' for a failed conversion

**Cons:** Runtime cost on every conversion: TypeId hashing, map lookup, boxing/Any-downcast, dyn dispatch — violates the spirit of invariant 2 (#2 low overhead) on a path the trait approach makes free; mitigated only by caching; Type erasure pain: ErasedValue = Box<dyn Any> means heap allocation per converted value and a fallible downcast; against the stack-over-heap / minimal-Arc discipline (invariant 5); Failure mode moves from compile-time to runtime: a missing converter for a field type is only discovered during the startup binding pass, not at compile time — weaker than Realization 1 on invariant 9 timing (though still a fail-fast startup pass, acceptable per the charter's tiered preference); Needs a shared, likely Arc'd, registry consulted concurrently during parallel bean init — risks a shared read-mostly structure (manageable with an immutable frozen map after refresh, but it IS shared mutable state during the registration window — global-lock-adjacent, invariant 5); Const TypeId keys help build the table but the value side is unavoidably dynamic; enum case-insensitivity and unit grammar must be hand-coded inside converters rather than leaning on Rust's type system

**Mechanisms considered:** Runtime registry bean: HashMap<(TypeId,TypeId), Arc<dyn Converter>> frozen after refresh; const TypeId::of (stable 1.91) to build registry rows as const descriptors; Box<dyn Any + Send + Sync> / Arc<dyn Any> erased value channel with downcast (stable since 1.0/1.29); Trait upcasting (stable 1.86) to view a Converter as supertrait for diagnostics; GenericConverter predicate converters for src/tgt ranges; Converter beans discovered via the same link-time/registry substrate the catalog defers (linkme/inventory as CANDIDATE backends for converter contribution)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is the realization that actually needs cross-crate discovery: 'a converter defined in any linked crate becomes available' is the Spring classpath analogue. That pulls in the full link-time hazard surface from the cross-crate doc — linkme (zero-cost, DCE-sensitive, no wasm) vs inventory (DCE-robust, wasm, life-before-main) vs build-time codegen vs explicit registration. Per the doc, register THIN const descriptors (TypeId pair + fn pointer to a const-constructible converter factory), never live converter objects, and resolve/instantiate at runtime; defer the substrate choice to Phase 2. Layer-0/DCE applies: a converter-only crate the binary never references could silently vanish, so converter contribution must ride the same scoped, force-linked discovery leaf chooses for components — NOT an implicitly-global pool (honoring the 'scope discovery' guardrail). Note the dual-classpath candidate: static link-time converter descriptors PLUS an optional dynamic directory-scanned/WASM-module converter source could both feed one registry; both are candidates, not decisions. Built-in converters live in leaf-core and are registered explicitly (no discovery hazard).

**T2 — execution context:** Registration window is at/just-after refresh (cold path): built-in converters added synchronously, user converter contributions collected from the (deferred) discovery substrate. If discovery is inventory-based, registration descriptors are emitted life-before-main and must be trivial/non-async/non-panicking — but the actual converter construction is deferred to the runtime registration pass (per the cross-crate doc's 'register descriptors not live objects'). After refresh the registry is frozen and read-only, so concurrent conversion during parallel/background bean init needs no lock and is non-blocking. Conversion itself is synchronous CPU work; convert() must never block or do async I/O (it runs inside bean wiring). Errors propagate as ConvertError Results; cancellation is a non-issue for the bounded pure conversion, but the discovery/registration pass participates in the structured startup sequence and aborts the refresh on a malformed converter contribution.

#### serde-Deserializer bridge — config tree as a self-describing Deserializer, conversions via Deserialize
Reframe binding+conversion as deserialization: leaf's origin-tracked config tree (a ConfigValue tree assembled from property-sources) exposes a `serde::Deserializer`. Conversion is then whatever `T: Deserialize` already does, plus leaf-provided Deserialize-compatible newtypes for the Spring grammar (Duration/DataSize/Period parse from a string in their Deserialize impl; enums use serde's case handling; collections/maps are native serde). @ConfigurationProperties on a struct = `T::deserialize(LeafDeserializer::new(subtree, ctx))`. @Value on a scalar = deserialize a single node. Relaxed-binding (the kebab/camel/SNAKE key-form mapping owned by the relaxed-binding neighbour) is handled by the Deserializer's key matching, not by conversion. Custom 'converters' are custom Deserialize impls or serde `#[serde(deserialize_with)]` hooks. Unit-defaulting is carried in ConvertCtx threaded through a custom Deserializer that the leaf newtypes read via a thread/ctx-scoped hint, or via wrapper types like `Seconds<u64>`.

**Pros:** Leverages the entire serde ecosystem: every type that is already Deserialize is convertible for free, dramatically widening built-in coverage with near-zero leaf code (strong DX for the common case, invariant 1); No leaf-specific conversion trait to learn for most users — 'it's just serde' — and serde's derive is the canonical Rust config-mapping idiom; Stable, mature, zero-nightly; serde is ubiquitous so MSRV/portability is a non-issue including wasm; Origin-agnostic and source-agnostic: the Deserializer wraps an opaque ConfigValue tree, so any value origin (file, env, WASM module) that produces the tree works identically; Collections/maps/nested objects come from serde natively — directly matches Spring's list/set/array/map binding without bespoke collection-conversion code

**Cons:** Impedance mismatch with Spring's grammar: Duration/DataSize suffix parsing, @DurationUnit default units, and case-insensitive enums are NOT serde defaults — they require custom Deserialize impls or deserialize_with, and threading unit-context through serde's stateless Deserializer is awkward (serde has no clean per-field context channel), risking thread-local/ctx hacks that fight invariant 3's execution-context discipline; Diagnostics: serde's error messages are generic ('invalid type: expected u64') and lose leaf's origin/provenance and 'which property, which file:line' richness unless leaf writes a custom Deserializer that re-wraps every error — significant work to meet invariant 9; serde conflates 'parse' and 'convert': you cannot easily express Spring's (src,tgt) converter graph or a runtime-pluggable conversion the way a registry can; extending conversion = writing Deserialize impls, with orphan-rule limits like Realization 1; Pulls serde into leaf-core's public surface as a semi-mandatory dependency for binding, coupling leaf's config model to serde's data model (a strategic dependency the charter would want weighed; relaxes 'opinionated core forces only its own'); Strict vs lenient policy and ignoreUnknownFields/ignoreInvalidFields map only loosely onto serde's deny_unknown_fields and error handling — leaf must layer policy atop serde rather than owning it

**Mechanisms considered:** Custom serde::Deserializer over the ConfigValue tree (primary); serde Deserialize derive as the binding mechanism for config-properties; #[serde(deserialize_with)] and wrapper newtypes (Seconds<T>, Bytes) for unit grammar; Custom DeserializeSeed to thread ConvertCtx/unit-hint without thread-locals; Error-wrapping Deserializer layer to re-attach origin-tracking provenance; Optional: keep serde behind a cargo feature so non-serde users can fall back to Realization 1's trait

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Conversion-by-Deserialize needs no cross-crate registry: a downstream Deserialize impl is visible wherever its type is, exactly like Realization 1, with zero DCE/linker exposure and full wasm support. The serde dependency resolves once via workspace version unification (the cross-crate doc's recommended pinning). No link-time discovery is involved for the core path, so Layer-0/--gc-sections hazards do not apply. The only cross-crate consideration is keeping the LeafDeserializer + leaf newtypes in leaf-core so their Deserialize impls are coherent and the emitted binder code can hard-code ::leaf_core paths (proc-macro hygiene). If Spring-style globally-discovered custom converters are ever wanted, that again requires bolting Realization 2's registry on top — candidate, not decided.

**T2 — execution context:** Deserialization is synchronous, CPU-only, non-blocking; runs in the startup binding/validation pass and at @Value resolution during bean construction — cold paths, safe inline on any async executor. No async, no I/O inside Deserialize impls (leaf must document that custom impls must not block). Errors are serde::de::Error values wrapped back into leaf's ConvertError with origin context and propagated up the startup diagnostics chain; the threading of ConvertCtx (unit hints, locale) must avoid thread-locals that don't survive .await — if context is needed it must be passed via DeserializeSeed or a borrowed ctx, NOT an ambient thread-local, to honor execution-context discipline. Bounded pure work, so no cancellation concern.

### Rust clashes
- Spring needs a runtime ConversionService precisely because the JVM erases generics and lacks compile-time reflection — the target type is often only known as a Class<?> at runtime. In Rust the target type is almost always statically known at the @Value/binding call site, so a runtime (TypeId,TypeId) registry is largely solving a problem Rust doesn't have. The clash: faithfully porting the registry reintroduces erasure + boxing that the type system would otherwise eliminate (invariant 2). Resolving this tension — trait-native vs runtime service — is the core decision and likely a Phase 2 unification call shared with the type-erasure/registry-substrate meta-concept.
- Orphan rule: Spring lets you register a converter for ANY (src,tgt) pair from anywhere. Rust's coherence forbids `impl ForeignTrait for ForeignType`, so a trait-native approach (Realizations 1/3) cannot add conversions for std/third-party target types without a leaf-owned newtype/wrapper or a runtime registry. There is no clean rust-native equivalent of 'register a converter for java.time.Duration from my app crate' when the target is foreign.
- No async Drop / async context discipline barely touches conversion (it's pure sync), but the unit-defaulting context (@DurationUnit, locale) wants to be 'ambient' the way Spring threads a ConversionService + locale — and Rust's idiomatic answer (thread-locals) does not survive .await. Passing ctx explicitly is required, which is more verbose than Spring's invisible threading (a DX-vs-discipline clash, invariants 1 vs 3).
- Spring's ConversionService is a single mutable bean populated during refresh then used everywhere; Rust prefers an immutable, frozen, lock-free structure. A faithful 'add a converter bean at runtime' registry is shared-mutable during the registration window, brushing against the no-global-locks discipline (invariant 5) unless frozen-after-refresh.
- Rich enum/Duration/DataSize grammar (case-insensitive, suffix units) is bespoke parsing that neither FromStr nor serde does by default — Rust gives no free lunch here; leaf must own these parsers as newtypes regardless of which realization, so the grammar lives in code, not in a declarative converter the way Spring annotations imply.
- 'Collections are replaced not deep-merged across sources' is a property-source/binder precedence rule, not a conversion rule — in Rust this must be enforced by the property-sources/binder layer before conversion sees a single resolved ConfigValue; conversion itself only ever sees one already-merged value, so the merge semantics cannot live in the conversion layer at all.

### Interactions
- **value-injection** — Primary consumer. @Value resolves a ${placeholder} to a raw string/ConfigValue, then converts it to the field/param's target type. leaf's @Value macro emits the conversion call (T::from_config_value / T::deserialize / conversion_service.convert::<T>). Must agree on the ConvertCtx (strict-vs-lenient policy mirroring Spring's lenient default + PropertySourcesPlaceholderConfigurer strict mode) and on origin propagation for diagnostics.
- **binder** — Primary consumer and the heaviest user. The binder walks a Bindable target tree and invokes conversion per leaf node; collection/map binding is co-owned (the binder structures children, conversion coerces leaves). Whichever realization wins, the binder is the main client API; bind-result diagnostics carry ConvertError. config-properties sits on top of binder and inherits the same conversion.
- **config-properties** — Indirect consumer via binder. The strongly-typed POJO/record fields' Rust types ARE the conversion targets; @ConfigurationProperties does NOT evaluate expressions (unlike @Value) so its conversion path is pure config-to-type with no expression-language involvement. Fail-fast validation depends on conversion errors surfacing at the startup binding pass.
- **relaxed-binding** — Adjacent, separation-of-concerns. relaxed-binding maps a source-specific key form (camelCase/SNAKE/index conventions) to the canonical kebab key BEFORE conversion; conversion sees an already-resolved single ConfigValue and never touches key spelling. Clear boundary: relaxed-binding = key identity, type-conversion = value coercion.
- **property-resolution** — Upstream supplier. Resolves ${...} placeholders and produces the raw string value that conversion consumes. The 'collections replaced not deep-merged' precedence rule lives here / in property-sources, not in conversion — conversion only ever sees the single highest-precedence merged value.
- **origin-tracking** — Diagnostics dependency. ConfigValue carries provenance (file/line/owning source); ConvertError must include it so a coercion failure reports 'cannot convert "abc" to u16 for property server.port (application.yaml:12)'. This is how conversion satisfies invariant 9's rich-context requirement.
- **expression-language** — Sibling on the @Value path only. #{SpEL}-style expressions evaluate to a value that may then need conversion to the target type; for @ConfigurationProperties expressions are deliberately NOT evaluated. The two layers compose (expression evaluates, then convert) but stay distinct; conversion does not depend on the expression engine.
- **validation** — Downstream sibling reused by binding. config-properties binding runs conversion THEN JSR-303-style validation; both fail fast at startup. Conversion catches type/format errors, validation catches semantic/range constraints. They share the startup fail-fast diagnostics surface but are separate passes (convert-then-validate).
- **autowiring-resolution** — Minor consumer (Spring's step-2 @Value shortcut in doResolveDependency). Most autowiring is by type and needs no conversion; conversion only enters when an injection point carries a @Value. Realization 2's dynamic registry is the only one that could also support a hypothetical convert-between-bean-types path, which autowiring does not currently need.
- **messages-i18n / locale-context** — Possible ctx input. Locale-sensitive parsing/formatting (number/date formats) would draw the current locale from the locale-context ambient holder via ConvertCtx. Surfaces the execution-context-discipline concern: locale must be passed explicitly, not via an .await-unsafe thread-local.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Is conversion a compile-time trait (monomorphized, zero-cost, target-type-static) or a runtime ConversionService registry (dynamic, introspectable, Spring-faithful) — or a blend where the trait path is default and a runtime registry is an opt-in fallback for the orphan-rule / dynamic-target cases? This is the keystone decision and is entangled with the deferred type-erasure & registry-substrate meta-concept.
- Should leaf adopt serde::Deserialize as the canonical binding+conversion mechanism (huge built-in coverage, ecosystem fit) at the cost of pulling serde into leaf-core's public surface and inheriting serde's weaker diagnostics — or keep a leaf-owned conversion trait independent of serde? Cross-cuts the binder, config-properties, and the 'opinionated core forces only its own' invariant.
- How is the conversion ConvertCtx (strict/lenient policy, unit defaults from @DurationUnit-equivalents, locale from locale-context) threaded through binding without an .await-unsafe thread-local? This shares the unresolved async context-propagation / ambient-holder meta-concept (T2) with locale-context and context-propagation.
- If custom converters can be contributed from other crates (Spring's @ConfigurationPropertiesBinding intent), do they ride the SAME scoped cross-crate discovery substrate leaf picks for components/auto-config (linkme vs inventory vs build-time codegen vs explicit), and how is the Layer-0/DCE silent-empty-registry hazard handled for a converter-only crate? Couples to the cross-crate composition meta-concept and the 'scope discovery, don't make it global' guardrail.
- Where exactly does conversion sit in the fail-fast timing ladder (invariant 9): compile-time (trait approach catches missing impls), a dedicated startup binding/validation pass (registry approach), or runtime — and is that boundary consistent across @Value vs @ConfigurationProperties? Shares the unified error/diagnostics meta-concept.
- Who owns the orphan-rule escape hatch for converting to foreign/std target types — a leaf-provided Conv<T> newtype, a #[derive], or only the runtime registry — and does that choice force the registry to exist regardless of the default mechanism?
- Should the built-in Spring-grammar types (Duration/DataSize/Period) be leaf-owned newtypes (controllable grammar, but a new type users must adopt) or impls layered onto std::time::Duration / a community type (familiar, but grammar must coexist with that type's existing FromStr/Deserialize)? Affects DX and the orphan rule.

### Notes
Strongest rust-native fit is Realization 1 (trait-native): it turns Spring's runtime registry — which exists mainly to route around JVM erasure — into compile-time dispatch that Rust gets for free, best serving invariants 1/2/5/9, at the cost of the lowest Spring-mental-model parity and the orphan-rule friction. Realization 2 (runtime registry) is the highest-parity but reintroduces exactly the erasure/boxing/shared-mutable-state that invariants 2 and 5 push against; its real value is the dynamic/general-converter case and the introspectable single service, which the trait approach cannot offer. Realization 3 (serde bridge) is a pragmatic DX win for coverage but couples leaf-core to serde and fights leaf's rich-diagnostics goal. A likely Phase-2 synthesis: trait-native as the default zero-cost path, serde as an optional built-in bridge feature, and a thin optional runtime registry only for the genuinely dynamic / orphan-rule cases — but that unification is explicitly Phase 2/3's call, not made here. Note the recurring structural fact across all three: 'collections replaced not deep-merged' and key-form mapping are NOT conversion concerns (they belong to property-sources/binder/relaxed-binding); conversion only ever sees one already-resolved value — keeping the conversion layer narrow and pure is the cleanest invariant across realizations. The leaf-owned Spring-grammar types (Duration/DataSize/Period) and the case-insensitive-enum derive are needed regardless of mechanism and should live in leaf-core for coherence.

## MessageSource / i18n  `[messages-i18n]`

Spring's `MessageSource` is an `ApplicationContext`-only context service (one of the conveniences the façade layers over the bare `BeanFactory` engine, alongside events/resources/Environment). Its intent: resolve a localized, parameterized message from a stable string *code* plus an ordered list of *arguments* and a *Locale*, returning the formatted result — `getMessage(code, args, locale)`. The behavioral specifics worth replicating as INTENT (not mechanism): (1) it is a magic-named bean — the context looks for a bean named `messageSource` during refresh (`initMessageSource()`), and if none exists installs a no-op `DelegatingMessageSource` default; same magic-name pattern as `applicationEventMulticaster`. (2) It is hierarchy-aware: an unresolved code walks the parent context chain (a `DelegatingMessageSource`/`HierarchicalMessageSource` delegates to the parent's source), mirroring container-hierarchy's one-directional visibility (child shadows parent; parent never sees child). (3) The Locale input defaults to "the current locale" — Spring reads `LocaleContextHolder` (our locale-context neighbour) when no explicit locale is passed. (4) It supports `MessageSourceResolvable` (an object carrying its own codes+args+default), a default-message fallback, and a hard-fail mode (`NoSuchMessageException`) when a code is absent and no default given. (5) Arguments are formatted with locale-sensitive conversion (numbers, dates) — in Spring via `MessageFormat`. (6) Injectable into beans via `MessageSourceAware`, and the context itself implements `MessageSource` so it is "first-class i18n on the context."

leaf must realize this intent in async-first Rust: a context-level service that resolves `(code, args, locale) -> formatted string`, defaults the locale to the current ambient locale (locale-context), walks the context hierarchy on a miss, defaults to a usable-or-loud no-op when unconfigured, and exposes a rich diagnostic on an unresolved code. The catalog *source* (where bundles come from) must be ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC: native compiled-in catalogs are the default, but a dynamic directory-scanned / WASM-module catalog source must be able to slot in behind the same provider trait. Phase-1 placeholder name: `MessageSource`. This is implementation-agnostic — the realizations below diverge on *where the message catalog lives and when it is resolved* (compile-time-checked codes vs runtime registry vs layered provider chain), not on a meta-architecture pick.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Context-service trait + runtime catalog-provider chain (closest intent parity, dynamic-source ready)
A `MessageSource` trait is a context service the façade (ApplicationContext analogue, see container-core R1/R2/R3) exposes — the bare engine does NOT have it, exactly mirroring Spring's BeanFactory-vs-ApplicationContext split. Surface (DX-first, async only where a source can do I/O):

```rust
trait MessageSource: Send + Sync {
    // primary resolution; locale defaults to current ambient locale when None
    async fn message(&self, code: &str, args: &[Arg<'_>], locale: Option<&Locale>) -> Result<String, NoSuchMessage>;
    // resolvable-object form (carries its own codes+args+default)
    async fn resolve(&self, r: &dyn MessageResolvable, locale: Option<&Locale>) -> Result<String, NoSuchMessage>;
    // explicit default fallback (never errors)
    async fn message_or(&self, code: &str, args: &[Arg<'_>], default: &str, locale: Option<&Locale>) -> String;
}
```

The context holds ONE `MessageSource` handle (resolved at refresh: a magic-named `messageSource` bean if registered, else a `DelegatingMessageSource` no-op default that just echoes the code or the explicit default — the loud-but-usable fallback). Behind the configured source sits a `MessageCatalogProvider` trait — origin-agnostic — that yields `(code, locale) -> Option<MessagePattern>`:

```rust
trait MessageCatalogProvider: Send + Sync {
    async fn lookup(&self, code: &str, locale: &Locale) -> Option<MessagePattern>;
    fn name(&self) -> &str; // for diagnostics
}
```

A `CatalogChain` composes providers in priority order (first match wins, locale-fallback de_DE→de→root applied within each). Native compiled-in bundles are one provider; a directory-scanned/WASM-module provider (see T1) is just another `MessageCatalogProvider` slotted into the chain — the resolver can't tell native from dynamic. Hierarchy: the context's `MessageSource` wraps an `Option<parent MessageSource>`; on a miss after exhausting the local chain it delegates to the parent context's source (one-directional, child shadows parent). Locale defaulting: when `locale` is `None`, read the current locale from the locale-context holder (`LOCALE.get()`), keeping i18n decoupled from explicit locale threading. Formatting: `MessagePattern` is a parsed, locale-aware template (named/positional placeholders); argument coercion delegates to the type-conversion neighbour's locale-sensitive formatters (numbers/dates) — NOT a bespoke formatter. A thin `#[messages]`/`message!(code, args)` macro is pure sugar emitting a hand-writable `source.message(...)` call against the public API; it carries no catalog logic.

**Pros:** Highest intent parity: the magic-named-bean → default-no-op → hierarchy-walk → current-locale-default → rich-miss-error chain is reproduced almost beat-for-beat, so a Spring porter recognizes every behavior.; Origin-agnostic by construction: `MessageCatalogProvider` is the seam the brief demands — native, directory-scanned, and WASM-module catalogs are indistinguishable to the resolver, so a future dynamic 'classpath' of catalogs slots in with zero resolver changes (directly realizes the static+dynamic duality).; Runtime registry means codes need not be known at compile time — supports user-added locales, hot-reloadable bundles, and operator-supplied translations, the strongest match for real i18n workflows.; Async on the resolution method lets a dynamic/remote/WASM catalog do I/O on the cold lookup path without poisoning the trait into bimodality; compiled-in providers just return Ready, so no allocation forced for the common case if the future is monomorphized on the static path.; Hierarchy delegation is a thin `Option<parent>` wrap — reuses container-hierarchy's exact visibility model rather than a bespoke mechanism (unification).

**Cons:** Codes are stringly-typed: a typo in `message!("oder.placd")` is not a compile error — it surfaces as a runtime `NoSuchMessage` (charter §2.9 prefers the richest-diagnostic *timing*; this defers to runtime). Mitigable by an optional startup validation pass (R3) but not by this realization alone.; Async-in-trait on a context service that is almost always stored as `dyn MessageSource` hits the AFIT dyn-incompatibility wall — the dyn path must box the future (`Pin<Box<dyn Future>>`), an alloc per resolution on the dynamic path; acceptable on a cold/error path, but message resolution can be hot (per-rendered-error, per-response), so the boxing cost is real and must be weighed.; A provider *chain* with locale-fallback per provider is more moving parts than a single map; ordering/priority is another runtime concern to get right (mitigated by treating priority as descriptor data + runtime sort, never link order).; Stores at least one `Arc<dyn MessageSource>` per context (charter §2.5 minimal-Arc tension), plus boxed catalog providers — heap for the catalog layer even when only compiled-in bundles are used.

**Mechanisms considered:** context-service trait exposed by the façade only (mirrors container-core's events/resources layering); magic-named `messageSource` bean lookup at refresh, else install a no-op DelegatingMessageSource default; origin-agnostic `MessageCatalogProvider` trait (native | directory-scanned | WASM-module) behind a priority CatalogChain; `Arc<dyn MessageSource>` with `Option<parent>` for hierarchy delegation; trait upcasting (1.86) to coerce concrete sources; AFIT on resolution; boxed future at the dyn boundary (trait_variant/async-trait shim) since the source is dyn-stored; delegate argument formatting to the type-conversion neighbour's locale-aware ConversionService rather than a private formatter; thin `message!`/`#[messages]` macro emitting only a public-API call (no catalog logic in the macro); locale defaulting by reading the locale-context holder when locale arg is None

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Message catalogs are a discovery problem with the same shape as component-scanning: bundles (`messages_de.ftl`/`.properties`-equivalent, or a `register_catalog!(...)` descriptor) are declared in whichever crate owns the feature's text — a web crate, a validation crate, the app crate — and the core must NOT hardcode them. So a catalog provider must self-register into a registry the context enumerates at refresh. That registration inherits the full cross-crate hazard set from the cross-crate doc: a linkme distributed-slice row (zero-cost, server targets) or inventory (DCE-robust, wasm) — CANDIDATES, decided in Phase 2 — and the Layer-0 trap (a translation-only crate the binary never path-references contributes an empty catalog, silently). The macro must emit a const, data-only catalog descriptor via absolute paths (`::leaf_core::CatalogDescriptor`), and the façade must run a self-check (expected-vs-found catalog count, or a manifest cross-check) failing loudly when an expected locale/bundle is missing — non-negotiable given silent DCE. CRITICALLY, this feature is the strongest natural fit for the static+dynamic duality the brief flags: the static link-time/build-codegen catalog set is the default 'classpath' of compiled-in translations, AND an optional dynamic directory-scanned source (drop `messages_*.ftl` or a `.wasm` catalog module into a configured dir, no recompile) is the dynamic 'classpath' — both feed ONE `MessageCatalogProvider` chain, NOT two code paths. The WASM-module exploration explicitly calls out hot-reloadable config/strategy plugins as a green-zone use; a translations module is exactly that. Compiled-in catalogs may also be emitted by build.rs codegen from resource files (sqlx-style), which sidesteps DCE entirely and is the portable wasm/embedded path.

**T2 — execution context:** Resolution runs on the caller's async task. Compiled-in catalog lookups are pure in-memory (a map + locale fallback) and do not block — safe on the (potentially hot) rendering path; the future is Ready immediately. A dynamic/directory/WASM provider may `.await` I/O (read a file, call across the WASM boundary) — that is a cold path (first lookup / cache miss) and must be documented to never block the executor (file I/O via the runtime's async fs or `spawn_blocking`; WASM via the host executor per the wasm exploration's WASI-0.3 async seam). Catalog loading itself happens at refresh (cold, single-threaded-ish startup) or lazily on first miss; loaded patterns are cached behind a per-locale read-mostly structure — read path is lock-free/reactive (no global lock; charter §2.4/§2.5), a refresh/reload is a cold-path swap. Locale read (`LOCALE.get()`) is a non-blocking ambient lookup (locale-context). Errors: an unresolved code with no default yields a rich `NoSuchMessage` carrying the code, the locale tried, the fallback chain walked, and the providers consulted (charter §2.9) — never a panic. Cancellation: a dropped resolution future just abandons the (idempotent) lookup; no partial state. No async Drop concern — catalog providers are read-only after load; a WASM provider's Store teardown rides the explicit container-driven shutdown (consistent with context-close).

#### R2 — Compile-time-checked message codes via a typed catalog (codes are types/consts, not strings)
Invert the stringly-typed default: make message codes a checked, typed vocabulary so a missing/misspelled code is a *compile* error wherever the compiler can give a legible one (charter §2.9 'as early as the richest diagnostic allows'). A bundle is declared once (e.g. a `messages.ftl`/`.toml` resource), and a build.rs/proc-macro emits a typed accessor module per bundle: each code becomes a generated `const`/fn with a typed argument signature derived from the template's placeholders.

```rust
// generated from order.ftl: "order.placed = Order {id} placed for {amount}"
mod msg {
  pub struct OrderPlaced<'a> { pub id: u64, pub amount: &'a Money }
  impl Message for OrderPlaced<'_> { const CODE: &str = "order.placed"; fn args(&self) -> ... }
}
// call site — wrong field name / wrong type is a COMPILE error:
ctx.messages().render(msg::OrderPlaced { id, amount }, None).await
```

The `MessageSource` context service now takes a typed `M: Message` rather than a bare `&str`, and `render` looks up the (compile-time-known) `M::CODE` in the locale catalog. The catalog at runtime is still a map (translations for non-default locales are loaded data), but the *code set and argument arity/types* are frozen at build time. Untranslated-at-runtime is still possible (a locale missing a key) → falls back to the default-locale template (compiled in) or a rich runtime error, but you can never reference a code that does not exist or pass the wrong arguments. A `dyn`-friendly escape hatch (`message_str(code, args)`) remains for dynamic/user-supplied codes (the R1 path), so the typed layer is additive, not exclusive. Hierarchy + current-locale-default + no-op-default behave as in R1.

**Pros:** Richest diagnostic timing for the common case: a typo or wrong-typed argument fails at compile time with a legible error (the generated accessor is plain Rust), exactly what charter §2.9 prefers — no waiting for runtime to discover `order.placd` is missing.; Argument type-safety: placeholders become typed fields, so 'passed a string where the template formats a number' is caught up front; eliminates a whole class of MessageFormat runtime surprises Spring has.; Zero-ambiguity refactors: renaming a code is a compiler-checked change across the workspace; IDE autocomplete lists available messages — strong DX win.; The default-locale template is compiled in, so the no-translation-loaded path always has a usable string (the loud-but-usable fallback is structural, not a runtime branch).; Still composes with R1's runtime provider chain for *translations* and for genuinely dynamic codes, so it is a typed *front* over the same origin-agnostic catalog substrate — not a separate world.

**Cons:** Heaviest codegen and a build step (build.rs or a fat proc-macro reading resource files) — tension with the thin-macro invariant (§2.10): the macro/codegen now embeds template parsing + arg-type inference, which is real logic, not just emission. Must be carefully framed as 'emits what you could hand-write' (a struct + a const + an args fn) with the parsing in a normal testable crate.; Cross-crate code identity: a generated `msg::OrderPlaced` type lives in the crate that owns the bundle; consuming it cross-crate is fine (ordinary types, no link magic) — but it means the *code vocabulary* is fixed at build time and cannot be extended by an operator-supplied bundle at runtime (the dynamic-translations use case must fall back to the `message_str` escape hatch, losing the type-check there).; Locale-specific translations are still runtime data, so 'this key is missing in `fr`' remains a runtime/startup concern — compile-time checking only covers the code set and the default-locale template, not translation completeness across locales (that needs R3's startup pass).; Generics/monomorphization: a generated typed message with generic args has no single symbol; mostly a non-issue (codes are concrete) but template-with-generic-argument cases need a concrete shim.; Couples the i18n authoring DX to a build/codegen pipeline, which is rougher on wasm/embedded (though build.rs codegen is actually the *portable* substrate per the cross-crate doc, so this can be a pro on those targets).

**Mechanisms considered:** build.rs / proc-macro codegen emitting one typed accessor (struct + const CODE + args fn) per message from a resource bundle; `Message` trait with `const CODE: &'static str` (stable const since 1.91 era) keying into the runtime catalog; typed `render<M: Message>(m, locale)` front over the same runtime `MessageCatalogProvider` substrate as R1; additive `message_str(code, args)` dyn escape hatch for runtime/operator-supplied codes (preserves R1's dynamic path); compiled-in default-locale templates as the structural loud-but-usable fallback; optional `--check`-able catalog manifest (sqlx-offline style) so CI catches drift between code and bundles

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is the build-time-codegen architecture (C in the cross-crate doc) applied to i18n, and it is the most reliable/portable substrate: a crate's build.rs reads its OWN bundle files (the one thing build.rs can always see) and emits typed accessors + a const catalog table into OUT_DIR — no link-time slice, no DCE, no Layer-0 trap for the *default-locale* templates and code set, works identically on wasm/embedded. The generated message types are ordinary cross-crate items (trait-system reachable), so a consumer crate using `other_crate::msg::OrderPlaced` is statically linked correctly by reference — no force-link discipline needed for the typed path. The residual cross-crate surface is *runtime translation bundles* for additional locales: those still want a registry (linkme/inventory/dir-scan) to be discovered across crates, inheriting the same DCE/Layer-0/self-check hazards as R1 — so this realization narrows the hazard to the translation-only layer rather than eliminating it. A `cargo leaf prepare`-style checked-in manifest (sqlx model) can cross-check that every code referenced in the binary has a default template and flag missing-locale gaps in CI. The dynamic WASM/directory catalog still attaches via the `message_str`/provider escape hatch (origin-agnostic), so the duality is preserved but the *typed* half is statically frozen.

**T2 — execution context:** Codegen and template parsing run at build time on the host (cold, offline) — zero runtime cost and no execution-context question. At runtime, `render<M>` is a const-code lookup into the in-memory catalog: pure, non-blocking, hot-path-safe; the default-locale template is always available without I/O. Loading non-default-locale translations is the same cold-path async/lazy load as R1 (file/remote/WASM, never block the executor; cache read-mostly, lock-free read). Locale defaulting reads the ambient holder (non-blocking). Errors: because the code and arg types are compile-checked, the only runtime failure is 'this locale lacks this key' → falls back to the compiled-in default template (no error) or, if strict mode is on, a rich `NoSuchMessage` naming the code+locale+fallback chain. No new cancellation/async-Drop surface beyond R1's translation-load path.

#### R3 — Resolver as a unified post-processor over a descriptor table, with a startup validation pass (dogfoods the container machinery)
Treat i18n not as a bespoke service wired by hand but as a *dogfooded instance of the container's own discovery + post-processing + startup-validation machinery* (charter §2.11 unification, and the container-core R3 'context-extension' shape). Catalog bundles are contributed as ordinary descriptors into the same origin-agnostic registry the rest of leaf uses (the static link-time set + optional dynamic dir/WASM set). A `MessageSourceInitializer` is an Infrastructure-role context extension (post-processor analogue) that, during the fixed-order refresh template (refresh-lifecycle), runs the 'init message source' phase: it (1) auto-detects whether a user registered a magic-named `messageSource` source — if so, uses it; else assembles a default source from the collected catalog descriptors; (2) folds in the parent context's source for hierarchy; (3) runs a *startup validation pass* over the collected codes/locales (configurable: warn or fail) that surfaces missing-translation gaps with full context BEFORE traffic — the dedicated startup-validation timing §2.9 calls for, sitting between compile-time (R2) and pure-runtime (R1). The runtime `MessageSource` surface is the same as R1 (string codes, async resolution, current-locale-default, rich miss error), but its *assembly and validation* reuse the container's own post-processor + descriptor-table + topo-ordering + self-check primitives rather than a private path. The catalog providers remain origin-agnostic; the dynamic WASM/dir source is just another descriptor source folded in by the same initializer (it is literally a ContextExtension in the R3 container shape).

**Pros:** Maximal unification: catalog discovery rides the SAME registry/descriptor substrate as component-scanning/post-processor-spi/auto-configuration; the message-source init is the SAME 'auto-detect magic-named-bean-or-install-default' pass the façade already runs for events/multicaster — one mechanism, many features (charter §2.11).; Best diagnostic *timing* tradeoff: the startup validation pass reports missing locales/keys with the full causal chain (which catalogs were found, which locales each covers, which codes lack a translation) at boot — the §2.9-preferred 'dedicated startup pass' that R1 lacks and that R2 cannot give for translation completeness across locales.; The infrastructure self-check (expected-vs-found catalog descriptors) is the same DCE-defense the façade runs for other infrastructure, so the silent-DCE risk is handled by shared machinery, not a one-off.; Origin-agnostic to the extreme: a WASM-module catalog is just another ContextExtension/descriptor source the initializer folds in — exactly the brief's 'two descriptor sources feeding one registration API' duality, here with no bespoke i18n plumbing.; Keeps the runtime resolver surface identical to R1, so it can layer R2's typed front on top later without rework — R3 is about *assembly/validation*, orthogonal to the call surface.

**Cons:** Most indirection and the biggest Phase-1 over-reach risk: modeling i18n as a context-extension/post-processor pre-supposes the container adopts that shape (container-core R3), which is itself a deferred Phase-2 call — so this realization is partly contingent on a meta-architecture decision it must NOT make. Must stay a candidate, not a commitment.; The startup validation pass eagerly enumerates the cross-product of codes×locales — cost grows with catalog size; for very large message sets this is real boot work (mitigable: validate only configured/active locales, or make it opt-in like Spring's lazy default).; Heaviest coupling to as-yet-undecided neighbours (refresh-lifecycle ordering, the descriptor/registry substrate, the post-processor SPI) — if any of those shift in Phase 2, this realization's shape shifts with them.; Still stringly-typed at the call site (inherits R1's runtime-typo con) unless combined with R2.; Boxed-future-at-dyn-boundary cost (same as R1) for the resolution surface remains.

**Mechanisms considered:** i18n as a dogfooded Infrastructure-role context extension / post-processor in the fixed-order refresh template (init-message-source phase); catalog bundles contributed into the SAME origin-agnostic descriptor registry as components/auto-config (linkme/inventory/build-codegen — Phase 2 substrate); auto-detect magic-named `messageSource` source else assemble-from-descriptors default (the same pass the façade runs for the event multicaster); dedicated startup validation pass over codes×active-locales with warn/fail modes (the §2.9 'startup timing' diagnostic); shared infrastructure self-check (expected-vs-found catalogs) reusing the container's DCE-defense; runtime topo/priority sort of catalog providers as descriptor data (never link order); parent-context source delegation reusing container-hierarchy

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Identical substrate to R1/R2 but explicitly unified: catalog descriptors flow through the one registry the whole framework uses, so leaf solves the cross-crate discovery + DCE + Layer-0 + self-check problem ONCE for all discovery features and i18n inherits it. The static link-time/build-codegen catalog set is the default 'classpath'; the dynamic directory-scanned/WASM-module catalog source is folded in by the same initializer as an additional ContextExtension/descriptor source — the brief's static+dynamic duality realized as two descriptor sources, one registration API, zero bespoke i18n code paths. Force-linking a translation-only crate is the same generated `enable!`/force-link discipline as any contribution crate; the startup self-check turns a silently-dropped catalog into a loud boot error. Because assembly is a runtime pass over a flat descriptor table, ordering/priority/conditions (e.g. a locale only active under a profile) are runtime data, never link order — and a profile-gated catalog composes with the conditions/profiles neighbours for free.

**T2 — execution context:** The init-message-source phase runs during refresh (cold path, on the app's runtime, under the refresh driver) — it may `.await` to load catalogs (async fs / WASM host calls; never block the executor, document spawn_blocking for sync sources). The startup validation pass runs once at boot (cold) and aggregates all missing-key/locale findings into one rich report before completing refresh (fail-fast all-or-nothing if in strict mode, consistent with refresh's eager-fail semantics). Steady-state resolution is the same as R1: non-blocking in-memory read on the hot path, reactive cache (no global lock), cold-path async load on miss/reload. Cancellation of refresh drops the half-assembled source (no partial escape); teardown of a WASM-catalog Store rides the explicit container-driven shutdown (no async Drop), same as context-close. Errors carry the full chain (catalogs found, locales covered, code+locale tried) per §2.9.

### Rust clashes
- No magic-named-bean-by-type scan: Spring finds the `messageSource` bean by its magic string name during refresh and installs a `DelegatingMessageSource` default otherwise. Rust has no runtime by-name bean scan over a classpath; this becomes a runtime lookup in the container's name map (bean-naming) for a reserved name, plus a default-install branch in the refresh template — the 'magic name' is a reserved-name convention on the registry, not introspection.
- Stringly-typed codes vs Rust's type system: Spring resolves `getMessage(String code, ...)` — codes are opaque strings checked only at runtime. Idiomatic Rust wants typed, compile-checked codes (R2), but real i18n also needs runtime-extensible/operator-supplied codes (R1), and the two pull opposite ways — the design must offer the typed front AND the dynamic escape hatch, they cannot be the same artifact.
- Async-fn-in-trait is not dyn-compatible, but the MessageSource is almost always stored as `dyn` (it's a replaceable context service and must accept a WASM/dynamic origin). So the resolution method, if async (needed for dynamic/I/O-backed catalogs), must box its future at the dyn boundary (`Pin<Box<dyn Future>>`) — an alloc per resolution on the dyn path, on what can be a hot rendering path. Zero-cost async + dyn dispatch cannot both hold; the design must split a monomorphized typed-source fast path from the boxed dyn path.
- No global classpath / runtime reflection for catalog discovery: Spring's `ResourceBundleMessageSource` enumerates `basename_<locale>.properties` off the classpath. Rust has no classpath to scan; catalog bundles declared in arbitrary crates must self-register into a link-time/codegen registry that inherits the silent-DCE and Layer-0 'unreferenced crate contributes nothing' hazards — a translations-only crate the binary never path-references silently yields an empty catalog with no error.
- Locale value identity / formatting: Spring leans on JVM `Locale` + `MessageFormat` (ICU-grade, GC'd, reflective). Rust has no std locale/ICU; argument formatting (locale-sensitive numbers/dates/plurals) must be delegated to the type-conversion neighbour's ConversionService or an ICU-style crate, and `Locale` is a value type the design must define/borrow rather than reach for a global.
- GC'd shared catalog vs ownership: Spring's MessageSource and its loaded bundles are GC-rooted and freely aliased. Rust must pick a sharing model for the catalog (likely `Arc<dyn MessageSource>` + a read-mostly per-locale map), committing to refcount (charter §2.5 minimal-Arc tension) and `Send+Sync` bounds; the keystone scope/ownership decision (deferred) governs whether resolution returns an owned `String`, a borrow, or an `Arc<str>`.
- No async Drop for a dynamic/WASM catalog source: a directory-watcher or WASM-module catalog provider holds resources (file handles, a Wasmtime Store) whose teardown may be async; Rust has no async Drop, so cleanup must ride the explicit container-driven `shutdown().await` (context-close), not Drop — the container owns the catalog-source lifecycle as a hard discipline.
- Hierarchy delegation without inheritance: Spring's `DelegatingMessageSource`/`HierarchicalMessageSource` walks the parent via interface inheritance. Rust models this as an explicit `Option<parent>` field and manual delegation (HAS-A, like container-core's façade), reusing container-hierarchy's one-directional visibility rather than any subclassing.

### Interactions
- **locale-context** — The defining input relationship: when `message(code, args, None)` is called with no explicit locale, the MessageSource reads 'the current locale' from the locale-context LOCALE holder — exactly Spring's MessageSource ↔ LocaleContextHolder coupling. messages-i18n is the canonical *consumer* of the locale holder; it must depend on locale-context's read API but stay decoupled from how the locale is bound/propagated (that is locale-context + context-propagation's job).
- **container-core** — MessageSource is an ApplicationContext-only context service the façade exposes (the bare engine lacks it) — the same attach question container-core flags for events/resources. The magic-named-`messageSource`-bean resolution and the install-default-if-absent branch live on the façade's refresh, not the bare engine; whether it is an always-present service (R1-style) or an attachable capability (container-core R2/R3) is inherited from container-core's chosen shape.
- **container-hierarchy** — Hierarchy-awareness is core to the feature: an unresolved code walks the parent context chain. messages-i18n reuses container-hierarchy's one-directional visibility (child source shadows parent; parent never sees child) via an explicit `Option<parent MessageSource>` delegation rather than reinventing it.
- **refresh-lifecycle** — The 'init message source' phase (locate magic-named bean or install default) is a fixed step in the refresh template — directly analogous to Spring's `initMessageSource()` running before listeners/singletons. R3 makes the MessageSourceInitializer an ordered Infrastructure post-processor in that template; the startup validation pass also runs here (fail-fast at boot).
- **type-conversion** — Argument formatting (locale-sensitive numbers, dates, durations, sizes) delegates to the type-conversion ConversionService/formatter registry rather than a private formatter — unification: the same coercion machinery @Value/binding/autowiring use formats message arguments. This is the substrate that replaces Spring's MessageFormat.
- **aware-callbacks** — Injecting the MessageSource into beans that need it mirrors Spring's MessageSourceAware (one of the context-aware group fired before init). The framework may inject the source (or an accessor) into infrastructure/handler beans that declare a need — the i18n service is container infrastructure a bean can be made aware of.
- **events** — Sibling ApplicationContext-only context service with the identical magic-named-bean (`applicationEventMulticaster` vs `messageSource`) + install-default pattern; both are attached/auto-detected by the same façade refresh pass. Whatever assembly mechanism container-core picks for events applies equally here — strong unification target.
- **validation** — JSR-303-style constraint violations carry message codes resolved against a MessageSource (Spring's MessageInterpolator backs onto MessageSource). validation is a key downstream consumer of i18n for localizing constraint messages; the resolvable-object form (`MessageResolvable`) is exactly how a constraint violation presents its codes+args+default.
- **resource-loading** — Loading message bundles from classpath/file/URL resources (the `.properties`/`.ftl` analogues) goes through the resource-loading abstraction the context exposes — the catalog provider for compiled-in/directory bundles is a consumer of ResourceLoader, and the dynamic directory-scanned catalog source uses pattern-resolving resource access.
- **component-scanning** — Catalog discovery is the same descriptor-registry + DCE-defense + self-check problem as component-scanning; the static link-time catalog set is the analogue of the scanned 'classpath' and the dynamic directory/WASM source is the analogue of a runtime classpath — R3 explicitly unifies them onto one registry substrate (shared with auto-configuration and post-processor-spi).
- **conditions** — A catalog/locale can be conditionally active (only under a profile, only when a locale is configured); condition evaluation over the collected catalog descriptors at runtime decides which catalogs wire up — i18n composes with the conditions/profiles model rather than gating at compile/link time.
- **context-close** — A dynamic/directory-watching or WASM-module catalog source holds resources whose teardown (file watchers, a Wasmtime Store) cannot ride async Drop; context-close drives an explicit `shutdown().await` over the MessageSource's providers in the symmetric teardown path.
- **context-propagation** — Because the locale defaulting reads the ambient locale holder, the locale must survive thread/task hops; messages-i18n depends transitively on context-propagation moving the locale-context holder across `.await`/spawn so a resolution after an async hop still sees the right locale.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Diagnostic timing for missing/typoed codes (charter §2.9): compile-time typed codes (R2), a dedicated startup validation pass over codes×active-locales (R3), or pure-runtime NoSuchMessage (R1) — likely a blend (typed front + startup pass + runtime escape hatch), but which is the default, and how does the typed-codegen path reconcile with runtime-extensible/operator-supplied codes that cannot be type-checked? Touches the metadata/codegen-boundary deferred decision.
- Async-across-dyn for the resolution surface: does leaf accept a boxed future on the dyn `MessageSource` path (alloc per resolution, on a path that can be hot — per-rendered-error/per-response) as standard, or push a monomorphized zero-cost typed-source fast path with dyn as the escape hatch? This is the framework-wide async-execution-model call (deferred §3), and message resolution is a concrete hot-path stress case for it.
- Catalog discovery substrate: same cross-crate registration question as every discovery feature (linkme distributed-slice vs inventory vs build-time codegen vs explicit registration) and the static-vs-dynamic-classpath duality (link-time/codegen default + optional directory-scanned/WASM-module dynamic source). Must a translation-only crate force-link, and how is 'which catalogs participate' expressed and self-checked? Shared with component-scanning, auto-configuration, post-processor-spi, locale-context's holder registry.
- Return type / ownership of a resolved message (the keystone scope/ownership decision): does `message(...)` return an owned `String`, an `Arc<str>`, or a borrow into the catalog? This drives the catalog's storage model (Arc<dyn>+read-mostly map vs arena) and its Send+Sync bounds, and whether a WASM-origin catalog can produce the same handle.
- Locale value model and locale-sensitive formatting: does leaf define its own `Locale` type, depend on an ICU-style crate, or thread it through type-conversion? How are plurals/gender/ordinals (ICU MessageFormat-class features) handled — delegated to type-conversion, a chosen i18n crate, or a leaf-native pattern format? Cross-cuts type-conversion and the broader 'how opinionated is the core' question.
- Where does i18n sit in the container shape: is it an always-present façade service, an attachable capability, or a dogfooded Infrastructure context-extension/post-processor (R3)? This is contingent on container-core's unresolved façade-vs-engine shape and the post-processor/refresh-lifecycle model — i18n cannot fix its own assembly shape until that lands.
- Hot-reload / dynamic catalog policy: if a directory-scanned or WASM-module catalog source is supported, is reload event-driven (file-watch → reactive cache swap, charter §2.4) and how does it interact with the read-mostly cache concurrency model, the no-global-lock invariant, and context-close teardown of the watcher/Store (no async Drop)? Shared with the leaf-wasm exploration's open resource-lifetime question.

### Notes
Confidence: high on intent. The Spring section is terse on MessageSource specifically (it is treated as one bullet in the ApplicationContext-superset list, with the magic-name pattern called out explicitly at line 1902 and the hierarchy-walk at line 186, and `initMessageSource()` in the refresh template at line 343/359), so I grounded the deeper mechanics (DelegatingMessageSource default, MessageSourceResolvable, NoSuchMessageException, LocaleContextHolder feeding it, MessageSourceAware) from the well-known Spring contract referenced at line 2771 — flagged as intent, not mechanism.

The three realizations are genuinely divergent on the axis that matters for THIS feature — *where the message catalog lives and when codes/translations are validated*: R1 (runtime provider chain, stringly-typed, dynamic-source-ready, closest Spring parity), R2 (compile-time-checked typed codes via codegen, richest diagnostic timing, build-step cost), R3 (dogfood the container's own discovery/post-processor/startup-validation machinery, maximal unification, most contingent on deferred decisions). They are NOT mutually exclusive — the likely Phase-3 convergence is a typed front (R2) over a runtime provider chain (R1) assembled and validated by shared container machinery (R3) — but I kept them as divergent candidates per the brief.

Three things to carry forward: (1) This feature is the single strongest natural home for the static+dynamic 'classpath' duality the brief asks every discovery feature to flag — compiled-in/codegen catalogs as the static default PLUS a directory-scanned/WASM-module catalog source as the dynamic 'classpath', both feeding ONE origin-agnostic `MessageCatalogProvider` chain. The leaf-wasm exploration explicitly greenlights hot-reloadable translation modules, so I treated origin-agnosticism as a fixed constraint across all three. (2) The locale-context coupling is load-bearing and bidirectional in dependency terms: i18n is the canonical consumer of the current-locale holder, which in turn depends on context-propagation surviving async hops — a missing locale propagation silently degrades i18n to the default locale, so this chain needs a self-consistent story in Phase 2. (3) Argument formatting must delegate to type-conversion, not grow a private formatter — this is the clearest unification win and avoids re-litigating locale-sensitive number/date formatting per feature.

I deliberately did NOT settle: the async-across-dyn boxing tradeoff (message resolution is a concrete hot-path stress case for the framework-wide decision), the diagnostic-timing default (compile vs startup vs runtime), the catalog discovery substrate, or the resolved-message ownership type — all surfaced as phase2Questions, several shared verbatim with container-core and locale-context so Phase 2 sees the cross-cutting pressure.

Naming: 'MessageSource'/'MessageCatalogProvider'/'CatalogChain'/'NoSuchMessage' are Phase-1 placeholders mirroring Spring; final names are later. I wrote no files. Relevant grounding paths (all absolute): /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/spring-boot-4-di-design.md (lines 49/112/128 superset+façade, 186 hierarchy-walk, 343/359 initMessageSource in refresh, 894/2494 MessageSourceAware in the aware group, 1902 magic-name pattern), /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-14-leaf-charter-design.md (invariants §2, deferred §3), /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/rust-cross-crate-composition.md (Architectures A–D, DCE layers 0/A/B, build-codegen sqlx model, scope-don't-globalize discovery), /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/rust-nightly-features-tradeoffs.md (Arc<dyn Any> registry, trait upcasting 1.86, AFIT/RPITIT dyn-incompat → boxed future at dyn boundary, const TypeId 1.91, no async Drop), /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/design/explorations/wasm-modules-for-leaf.md (dynamic directory-scanned catalog 'classpath', WASI-0.3 async seam, hot-reload green-zone, resource-lifetime open question).

## Resource Loading  `[resource-loading]`

Spring's `ResourceLoader`/`ResourcePatternResolver` is a context-exposed abstraction that uniformly names and opens artifacts regardless of origin. The intent has four load-bearing parts the leaf design must replicate (intent, not the JVM `ClassLoader` mechanism):

1. A uniform `Resource` HANDLE that decouples "what I want" from "where it lives": exists / is-readable / open-a-stream / get-a-URL-or-path / last-modified / a human description. Concrete origins (classpath entry, filesystem file, URL, in-memory bytes) all present the same surface, so consumers never branch on origin (Spring doc line 49/112/128: resource loading is one of the context-services the ApplicationContext façade layers over the bare engine).

2. Location STRINGS with protocol prefixes resolved by a single `getResource(location) -> Resource`: `classpath:`, `file:`, URL schemes, and a no-prefix form that defers to the context's default strategy. This is what makes `spring.config.import`, `banner.txt`/`spring.banner.location`, message bundles, and `@ConditionalOnResource` all speak one location grammar (lines 303, 1121, 1196).

3. PATTERN resolution — `ResourcePatternResolver.getResources(pattern) -> [Resource]` — including the `classpath*:` "scan every contributor" semantics plus Ant-style `**/*.class` globs. This is the engine under component-scanning's enumeration step (line 523: base package → `classpath*:` + pkg + `**/*.class` resolved via a `ResourcePatternResolver`) and under auto-config's `*.imports` discovery (line 1196: `getResources(...)` across all jars).

4. The loader is a CONTEXT SERVICE: the ApplicationContext IS-A ResourceLoader/ResourcePatternResolver, it is injectable into infrastructure beans (ResourceLoaderAware, and it sits in the resolvableDependencies map — line 705/894/2494), and it is handed to conditions via `ConditionContext.getResourceLoader()` (line 1121). The bare engine does NOT carry it; it is part of the façade superset.

The deep rust-native twist: Rust has NO classpath. The single most consequential intent-preserving move is to recognize that `classpath:` is, in Rust, a SYNTHETIC namespace — there is no runtime jar enumeration, so "classpath resources" must be either embedded at build time (`include_*`/build.rs/rust-embed-style) or contributed by linked crates through the same link-time/registry substrate leaf uses for components (the cross-crate doc's exact problem). `classpath*:` pattern scanning is the resource-shaped twin of component-scanning and inherits the identical Layer-0/DCE hazards and the static-vs-dynamic-source duality. So this feature is not "wrap std::fs"; it is "define an origin-agnostic, async-first resource abstraction whose `classpath:` arm is a registered/embedded namespace, whose `file:`/URL arms are real async I/O, and whose pattern resolver is honest about what it can and cannot enumerate per origin."

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Async `Resource` trait + protocol-keyed `ResourceLoader`, with `classpath:` as a build/link-time embedded namespace
Mirror Spring's two-trait shape directly but make it async-first and origin-agnostic. A `Resource` is an object-safe trait of cheap metadata accessors plus one async open: `fn description(&self) -> &ResourceId` (a typed origin+location, NOT a bare String), `fn exists(&self) -> ResourceExistence` (Known(true/false) or Unknown — see below), `fn last_modified(&self) -> Option<SystemTime>`, and the load-bearing async seam `async fn open(&self) -> Result<ResourceReader, ResourceError>` where `ResourceReader: AsyncRead + Unpin + Send` (or, for the common cold-path case, a convenience `async fn read_to_bytes(&self) -> Result<Bytes, ResourceError>`). `ResourceLoader` is the single-resource façade: `fn resolve(&self, loc: &Location) -> Result<Box<dyn Resource>, ResourceError>`, where `Location` is a PARSED type (scheme + path), not a string — leaf parses `classpath:`/`file:`/`http(s):`/bare into `Location` once, giving rich diagnostics on malformed locations rather than silent fallthrough. `ResourcePatternResolver: ResourceLoader` adds `async fn resolve_pattern(&self, pat: &Pattern) -> Result<Vec<Box<dyn Resource>>, ResourceError>`.

The scheme→handler map is the core data structure: `ResourceLoader` owns an ordered set of `ResourceProvider`s keyed by scheme, each a small object-safe trait `ResourceProvider { fn scheme(&self) -> Scheme; fn resolve(&self, loc) -> ...; async fn resolve_pattern(&self, pat) -> ... }`. Built-ins: a `FileResourceProvider` (real async fs via the runtime's fs API; pattern resolution = async directory walk + glob), a `UrlResourceProvider` (http(s) via an injected async client; pattern resolution = unsupported → a typed `PatternUnsupported(scheme)` error, mirroring Spring which also can't glob arbitrary URLs), and the keystone `ClasspathResourceProvider`. Because Rust has no classpath, `classpath:` resources are a SYNTHETIC namespace whose entries are registered descriptors: each is a `const ResourceEntry { logical_path: &'static str, bytes_fn: fn() -> &'static [u8] }` (or a fn-pointer to a lazily-mmapped file). A `#[resource("config/app.yaml")]`-style thin macro (or a build.rs codegen pass) emits one such const entry per embedded resource — exactly the hand-writable `include_bytes!`-backed static a user could write themselves (charter §2.10). `classpath:foo` is then an O(1) lookup over the registered entry table; `classpath*:**/*.yaml` is a glob over the entry table's logical paths — fully enumerable BECAUSE the table is a closed, link-time-collected set, not a real classpath.

The context exposes ONE `ResourceLoader` (the façade's resource service, per container-core); the bare engine has none. Injection points get `Arc<dyn ResourcePatternResolver>` via the resolvableDependencies seam. Conditions (condition-family's OnResource) and config-data and component-scanning all consume this one handle.

**Pros:** Tightest intent parity: `Resource`/`ResourceLoader`/`ResourcePatternResolver` map 1:1 onto Spring's three types, and the protocol-prefix grammar (`classpath:`/`file:`/URL/bare) is preserved, so the mental model ports cleanly and the same handle feeds scanning, config, and conditions.; Origin-agnostic by construction (brief's hard constraint): every consumer sees `dyn Resource`; a future WASM-module 'classpath' is just another registered `ResourceProvider`/entry-table source, indistinguishable to consumers — no consumer branches on origin.; Async-first and execution-context-honest: the only async seam is `open`/`resolve_pattern` (the real I/O); metadata accessors stay sync and cheap, so cold-path reads `.await` real I/O while hot-path existence checks on the embedded table are sync O(1).; `classpath:` as a closed embedded entry-table makes `classpath*:` pattern enumeration ACTUALLY POSSIBLE (the table is finite and known), unlike a real classpath — and sidesteps 'no runtime reflection' entirely.; Typed `Location`/`Pattern`/`ResourceId` (parsed, not stringly) gives rich diagnostics (§2.9): 'unknown scheme `claspath:` in location X (did you mean `classpath:`?)' instead of a silent miss.

**Cons:** `Box<dyn Resource>` per resolve is a heap alloc on the resolution path (charter §2.5 wants minimal boxing) — acceptable on the cold config/scan path, but a cost if anything resolves resources hot; an enum-of-known-origins could avoid it at the price of closed extensibility (kills origin-agnosticism).; `async fn open` on an object-safe `dyn Resource` hits the AFIT-not-dyn-compatible wall (nightly doc): the trait-object path must box the returned future (`Pin<Box<dyn Future>>`), an alloc per open. Tolerable for once-per-file reads, but it is a real cost and forces a `trait_variant`/boxed shim at the dyn boundary.; The embedded-`classpath:` table inherits the FULL cross-crate Layer-0/DCE hazard (cross-crate doc): a resource declared in a crate the binary never path-references contributes nothing, and `classpath*:` silently returns fewer hits — the exact silent-empty-registry failure, now for resources. Demands a self-check.; Two pattern-resolution capabilities that genuinely differ per origin (fs can glob, URL cannot, classpath-table can) means `resolve_pattern` must return a typed 'unsupported for this scheme' rather than a uniform guarantee — a leak of origin into the contract that Spring papers over.; `AsyncRead` as the reader bound couples the abstraction to a chosen async-I/O trait surface; if leaf stays runtime-agnostic (charter §2.6) the exact `AsyncRead` flavour (tokio vs futures) is itself a deferred decision this trait must not prejudge.

**Mechanisms considered:** thin `#[resource(...)]` proc-macro emitting one `const ResourceEntry` (include_bytes-backed static) per embedded classpath resource — hand-writable, zero macro logic; linkme distributed-slice OR build.rs codegen to collect `ResourceEntry`s across crates into the `classpath:` table (substrate-neutral; same A/B/C/D choice as components); object-safe `Resource`/`ResourceProvider` dyn traits + boxed `open` future at the dyn boundary (AFIT not dyn-compatible); scheme→`ResourceProvider` ordered map as the loader's core dispatch structure (file/url/classpath providers register the same way); parsed `Location`/`Pattern`/`Scheme` value types (not strings) for rich diagnostics; convenience `read_to_bytes` over the raw `AsyncRead` reader for the common cold-path slurp

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is the cross-crate-heavy realization. `file:`/URL providers are wholly local (no cross-crate concern). The `classpath:` namespace is the resource-shaped twin of component-scanning and inherits its entire substrate question: a `ResourceEntry` const emitted by a thin macro is collected across linked crates by WHATEVER substrate leaf picks (linkme slice A/B, build.rs codegen C, explicit `with_resources(...)` D) — this realization is deliberately substrate-NEUTRAL, it only fixes that entries are thin `const` fn-pointer-bearing descriptors hard-coding an absolute path to `leaf_core::ResourceEntry` (no proc-macro state, hand-writable). Layer-0 hazard is acute: a crate shipping only `#[resource]` declarations the binary never `use`s contributes zero entries, so `classpath:lib-default.yaml` silently 404s and `classpath*:` under-enumerates with NO error — the worst DX failure. Mitigation (non-negotiable regardless of substrate): a façade self-check that an expected-vs-found resource count / manifest cross-check fails loudly at startup (the cross-crate doc's mandated anti-silent-DCE defense). The static-vs-dynamic DUALITY the brief flags appears literally here: the link-time embedded entry-table is the default 'classpath', and an optional dynamic directory-scanned source (a `FileResourceProvider` pointed at a config dir, or a future WASM-module's resource table) is a SECOND provider feeding the same `resolve`/`resolve_pattern` API — two sources, one contract, NOT two code paths. Both are candidates, not a decision.

**T2 — execution context:** Loader construction and provider registration are synchronous cold-path (the `classpath:` table is const data; scheme map is built during façade bring-up). Metadata accessors (`exists` on the embedded table, `description`) are sync and non-blocking. The async seams are `open`/`read_to_bytes`/`resolve_pattern`: `file:` reads and directory globbing MUST use the runtime's async fs (or be documented to `spawn_blocking` if a blocking fs API is used — execution-context discipline §2.3); URL fetches `.await` a non-blocking client; `classpath:` reads of embedded bytes are effectively sync (return-ready future, no I/O) — a notable asymmetry the docs must state (a `classpath:` open never blocks; a `file:` open may). Cancellation: `open`/`resolve_pattern` futures are cancel-safe drop points — dropping a half-done directory walk or a partial read leaks nothing (no container-owned state, the reader owns its fd and Drop closes it). Errors propagate as a rich `ResourceError` carrying the parsed `Location`, the scheme, the provider that handled it, and the underlying io/http cause (§2.9): 'failed to open file:/etc/app.yaml (resolved from bare location `app.yaml` via FileResourceProvider): permission denied'. No global lock; providers are read-only after bring-up so resolution is lock-free and concurrency-safe.

#### R2 — Resources as a unification of property-sources: a `ContentSource` SPI shared with config-data / property-sources
Push charter §2.11 (unification) hard: observe that a `Resource` and a `PropertySource` are nearly the same thing — a NAMED, ORIGIN-TRACKED, lazily-opened bag of bytes/values. Rather than a bespoke ResourceLoader, define ONE low-level `ContentSource` SPI that BOTH resource-loading and property-sources/config-data/origin-tracking build on. A `ContentSource` is: `fn origin(&self) -> Origin` (file+line-capable, shared with origin-tracking), `fn id(&self) -> &ResourceId`, and `async fn bytes(&self) -> Result<Bytes, ResourceError>`. `Resource` then becomes a thin typed VIEW over a `ContentSource` (adds exists/last-modified/stream sugar); a `PropertySource` becomes a parsed view over the same `ContentSource` (adds key lookup after parsing the bytes as yaml/toml/env). The `ResourceLoader`/`ResourcePatternResolver` is a `ContentSourceResolver`: given a `Location`/`Pattern` it yields `ContentSource`s, and the resource feature wraps them as `Resource`, while config-data wraps the SAME ones as property sources. The scheme providers (`file`/`url`/`classpath`/the synthetic embedded table) are `ContentSourceProvider`s. Origin tracking is FREE and uniform — every resource carries provenance because `ContentSource` does (directly serving origin-tracking and §2.9 diagnostics). The context exposes a `ResourceLoader` view (Spring parity) but it is sugar over the shared resolver; config-data, conditions' OnResource, and component-scanning's enumeration all consume the resolver, and `config-data`'s `configtree:`/`env:` prefixes become just more registered `ContentSourceProvider` schemes — exactly the Spring `config-data` location-prefix model, now sharing the resource grammar.

**Pros:** Maximal unification (§2.11): resource-loading, property-sources, config-data location prefixes (`configtree:`/`env:`), and origin-tracking all sit on ONE content+origin primitive instead of four bespoke loaders — fewer concepts, one place to add a scheme, one provenance model.; Origin tracking falls out for free and uniformly: every resource and every property value already carries file/line/owning-source provenance because the shared `ContentSource` mandates `origin()` — directly advancing §2.9 rich diagnostics and the origin-tracking feature with no extra machinery.; A new scheme (`configtree:`, `env:`, a future `wasm-module:`) is added once as a `ContentSourceProvider` and instantly works for resources, config loading, AND conditions — the duality and extensibility the brief wants, expressed as one registry.; Smaller stable ABI surface: the cross-crate substrate only ever collects/contributes `ContentSource`-shaped descriptors, so the link-time registry is shared with config rather than duplicated — fewer registries to keep DCE-safe.; Strong fit with the v7 'config locations are a uniform prefixed-location space' direction (config-data §): leaf gets that model essentially for free because resources and config speak the same `Location` grammar.
