**Cons:** Over-unification risk and Phase-boundary risk: fusing resource-loading with property-sources/config-data PRE-JUDGES machinery that Phase 2/3 are meant to unify — this borders on declaring meta-architecture if taken as a decision rather than a candidate (must stay a candidate).; Couples this feature's fate to property-sources/config-data/origin-tracking: a churn in any of those ripples into the resource abstraction; the clean Spring separation (ResourceLoader knows nothing about properties) is deliberately broken.; `Resource` exposes streaming (`AsyncRead`, last-modified, large-file friendliness) that `PropertySource` (small parsed maps) does not need; forcing both through one `bytes()`-centric SPI either pessimizes large resources (slurp-to-`Bytes` is wrong for a 1GB file stream) or complicates the SPI with an optional streaming arm, eroding the 'one primitive' simplicity.; Risk of the lowest-common-denominator API: to serve both, `ContentSource` may end up neither a great resource nor a great property source — Spring kept them separate for a reason (a Resource can be a giant binary; a PropertySource is always small structured config).; Pattern/glob enumeration is a resource concern that property-sources don't have; the shared resolver still needs a resource-only `resolve_pattern`, so the unification is partial and the seam between 'shared content layer' and 'resource-only pattern layer' must be drawn carefully.

**Mechanisms considered:** one `ContentSource { origin, id, async bytes }` SPI as the shared substrate for resources AND property sources; `Resource` and `PropertySource` as thin typed views/newtypes over a `ContentSource`; `ContentSourceProvider` scheme registry shared with config-data's `configtree:`/`env:` prefixes; origin-tracking folded in as a mandatory `origin()` on every `ContentSource` (free provenance); optional streaming arm (`async fn stream() -> impl AsyncRead`) on `ContentSource` for large resources, defaulted to `bytes`-backed; same link-time/codegen substrate collecting `ContentSource` descriptors for both features (one registry)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Shares ONE cross-crate registry with config/property-sources, which is a pro (fewer DCE-vulnerable registries, one self-check covers both) and a coupling con. The embedded `classpath:`/config-content descriptors are collected by the same substrate-neutral mechanism as R1 (linkme A/B / build.rs C / explicit D), emitting thin `const` `ContentSource` descriptors with absolute paths to `leaf_core`. Layer-0/DCE hazard is identical to R1 but now a dropped contribution silently breaks BOTH a resource lookup AND any config that reads it — higher blast radius, so the self-check is even more load-bearing. The duality (static embedded table + dynamic directory/`configtree:` source + future `wasm-module:` source) is expressed as multiple `ContentSourceProvider`s feeding the one resolver — the cleanest expression of the brief's 'two sources, one API' among the three realizations, because config-data's own multi-prefix location model already wants exactly this shape. Still substrate-neutral; the A/B/C/D choice is deferred. Cross-crate ABI is smaller (one descriptor kind) but more central, so its stability matters more.

**T2 — execution context:** Same async seam placement as R1 but unified: `ContentSource::bytes()` is the single async I/O point, `.await`ing real fs/url I/O on the cold config/scan path and returning ready for embedded bytes. Because config-data loading runs during the façade's environment-preparation phase (Spring's EnvironmentPostProcessor stage, doc line 258) — BEFORE bean instantiation — the resolver must be usable very early (before most of the container exists), constraining it to depend only on the runtime + the embedded table + explicitly-passed dirs, not on resolved beans (an execution-ordering constraint config-data already imposes). Cancellation/errors: identical to R1 (cancel-safe `bytes()`, rich `ResourceError`+`Origin`). The shared-origin model means a config parse error and a resource read error carry the SAME provenance type, giving one consistent diagnostic shape across both features. No global lock; resolver/providers read-only post-bring-up. Large-file streaming, if added, must be explicitly NOT slurped — an execution-context note that the `bytes()` default is wrong for huge resources and a `stream()` arm must be used (else unbounded memory).

#### R3 — Capability-typed loader: zero-cost monomorphized resolution on the static path, `dyn` only as the dynamic escape hatch
Question whether the resource abstraction needs to be `dyn` at all on the common path. Most resource access in leaf is at KNOWN locations with KNOWN origins decided at compile/codegen time (config-data's declared locations, a bean's `#[resource("banner.txt")]`, a fixed message-bundle path). For those, generics + monomorphization give a zero-alloc, zero-dyn path; `dyn` is reserved for genuinely runtime-dynamic resolution (a location computed from a property at runtime, or the WASM-module source). So: a `Resource` is a TRAIT with an associated reader type and RPITIT async open (`trait Resource { fn exists(&self)->...; fn open(&self) -> impl Future<Output=Result<impl AsyncRead, ResourceError>>; }`) — zero-cost when the concrete type (`ClasspathResource`, `FileResource`) is known. Concrete resource structs are returned by typed constructors and by a typed loader: `loader.classpath("app.yaml") -> ClasspathResource`, `loader.file(path) -> FileResource`. A `#[resource("...")]` macro on a field/const can resolve to the concrete type at compile time, so a bean holding an embedded resource pays ZERO runtime resolution cost. THEN, layered on top, an object-safe `DynResource`/`dyn ResourceLoader` (with boxed `open` future) is the escape hatch for the dynamic path — built by a blanket `impl<R: Resource> DynResource for R`, and used by `ResourceLoader::resolve(&Location)` when the location is only known at runtime, by `ConditionContext.resource_loader()` (conditions are inherently dynamic/reflective-flavoured), and by the WASM-module origin. Pattern resolution lives only on the dyn/dynamic side (`resolve_pattern` is inherently runtime, returns `Vec<Box<dyn Resource>>`). This mirrors the charter/nightly-doc guidance to split a zero-cost monomorphized typed path from a boxed dyn path, applied to resources: the typed path is primary (best low-overhead), dyn is the honest escape hatch (best flexibility/origin-agnosticism).

**Pros:** Best low-overhead (#2): the common case — opening a known embedded/file resource — is fully monomorphized, no `Box<dyn Resource>` alloc, no boxed future, RPITIT zero-cost futures (nightly doc: RPITIT/AFIT are zero-cost on the static path); honors §2.5 (stack over heap, minimal boxing) on the hot/typed path.; Keeps origin-agnosticism AND a dyn escape hatch: the dynamic/runtime path and the WASM-module source still flow through `dyn ResourceLoader`/`Box<dyn Resource>`, so future dynamic origins slot in — the typed path is an optimization, not a closing of the door.; `#[resource("...")]` resolving to a concrete type at compile time can surface a MISSING embedded resource as a compile/codegen-time error for statically-named resources (§2.9 prefers the richest-diagnostic timing) — 'no embedded resource `classpath:banner.txt`' at build time instead of a runtime 404, partially dissolving the Layer-0 silent-miss for statically-referenced resources.; Cleanly separates the two genuinely different access modes Spring conflates: 'I know exactly what I want' (typed, compile-time) vs 'resolve this location/pattern I computed' (dynamic, dyn) — matching how leaf actually uses resources.; Pattern resolution being dyn-only is honest: globbing is inherently runtime and origin-variable, so paying the alloc there (cold path) while keeping single-known-resource access zero-cost is the right cost placement.

**Cons:** Most API surface / two-path cognitive load: users (and leaf's own code) must learn when they are on the typed path vs the dyn path; the generic `R: Resource` bound leaks into signatures of anything generic over resources, and crate-boundary APIs tend to want `dyn` anyway (pushing many real uses back onto the boxed path, eroding the zero-cost win).; RPITIT `open` returning `impl Future` is NOT dyn-compatible (nightly doc), so the `DynResource` escape hatch needs a SEPARATE boxed-future method — the blanket impl must adapt `impl Future` to `Pin<Box<dyn Future>>`, meaning leaf maintains two method shapes (typed `open` + boxed `open_boxed`) and the seam between them is real maintenance.; Compile-time resolution of `#[resource("...")]` to a concrete embedded type only works for the same-crate/path-referenced embedded case; cross-crate embedded resources STILL ride the link-time table and STILL have the Layer-0 hazard — so the 'compile-time miss detection' pro is partial and may give a false sense of safety.; Drifts furthest from Spring's single uniform `ResourceLoader.getResource` mental model — Spring users expect ONE loader returning ONE `Resource` interface; the typed/dyn bifurcation is a rust-native divergence that must be taught.; Generics-can't-be-registered tension (a charter clash): the typed path resists the link-time registry (a generic `Resource` impl has no single symbol to collect), so the embedded `classpath:` table must still be type-erased entries — the typed path and the registry path don't fully meet, and the boundary (typed view over an erased table entry) needs care.

**Mechanisms considered:** `Resource` trait with associated reader type + RPITIT `open` for the zero-cost monomorphized path; typed loader methods (`loader.classpath(..)`, `loader.file(..)`) returning concrete resource structs; `#[resource("...")]` macro resolving to a concrete type at compile/codegen time (compile-time miss detection for static names); object-safe `DynResource`/`dyn ResourceLoader` via blanket `impl<R: Resource>` with a boxed-future `open_boxed` adapter — the dynamic escape hatch; pattern resolution confined to the dyn/dynamic side (`Vec<Box<dyn Resource>>`), since globbing is inherently runtime; type-erased `ResourceEntry` table still backing `classpath:` (typed view reads from erased entries) — generics can't be link-registered

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The dynamic/dyn side is substrate-identical to R1/R2 (link-time/codegen-collected type-erased `ResourceEntry` table, Layer-0/DCE hazard, mandatory self-check). The novel cross-crate angle: the TYPED path interacts poorly with link-time registration — a monomorphized `ClasspathResource<typed>` has no stable symbol to collect across crates, so the cross-crate embedded table MUST remain type-erased entries, and the typed `#[resource]` macro can only give compile-time guarantees for resources whose bytes are embedded in or path-referenced by the SAME crate (`include_bytes!` locally). Cross-crate embedded resources fall back to the erased table and the runtime self-check. So this realization SPLITS the DCE story: same-crate static resources are compile-time-safe (a genuine improvement); cross-crate ones inherit the full hazard. The dynamic source (WASM-module / directory) is necessarily on the dyn side — origin-agnosticism is preserved only on the dyn path, which is acceptable since dynamic origins are by definition runtime. Substrate-neutral on the erased table; A/B/C/D deferred. The two-source duality lives entirely on the dyn `ResourceLoader` (static embedded table provider + dynamic directory/wasm provider), with the typed path being a same-crate fast lane over the static table.

**T2 — execution context:** Execution context bifurcates with the API. Typed path: `R::open` returns a concrete `impl Future`; for `ClasspathResource` over embedded bytes it is effectively sync/ready (no I/O, no block), for `FileResource` it `.await`s async fs — monomorphized, no boxing, the lowest-overhead async seam possible (§2.5/§2.3). Dyn path: boxed future per `open_boxed`/`resolve_pattern`, alloc on the cold dynamic path — acceptable because dynamic resolution and globbing are cold by nature. Cancellation: typed and dyn opens are both cancel-safe drop points (reader owns its fd; Drop closes). Pattern resolution (dyn-only) fans out async directory walks; dropping the future abandons the walk cleanly. Errors: rich `ResourceError` with parsed `Location`+scheme+provider on the dyn path; on the typed path the concrete type narrows the error set (a `ClasspathResource::open` can only fail with NotFound/embedded-corrupt, a `FileResource::open` with io::Error) — typed errors give even sharper diagnostics per §2.9. No global lock; loader read-only post-bring-up. Constraint: the typed path's compile-time resolution must run in the macro/codegen stage, so its 'fail early' benefit is a codegen-time event, not a runtime one — consistent with §2.9's richest-diagnostic-timing preference.

### Rust clashes
- No classpath, no runtime jar enumeration: Spring's `ResourceLoader` is fundamentally a `ClassLoader.getResource(s)` wrapper, and `classpath*:` literally walks every jar at runtime. Rust has neither. `classpath:` MUST be re-realized as a synthetic, CLOSED namespace whose entries are embedded at build time (`include_bytes!`/build.rs) and/or contributed by linked crates through leaf's link-time registry — and `classpath*:` pattern scanning becomes a glob over that finite collected table, NOT a filesystem/jar walk. The whole 'scan the classpath for resources' intent collapses into 'enumerate the registered/embedded resource entries,' inheriting the cross-crate doc's entire substrate problem.
- Link-time DCE silent-miss applies to RESOURCES, not just components: a crate that ships embedded `classpath:` resources but is never path-referenced by the binary contributes ZERO entries (Layer 0), and `--gc-sections`/reachability can drop entries (Layers A/B) — so a `classpath:lib.yaml` silently 404s and `classpath*:` silently under-enumerates with no error, in debug-passes-release-fails fashion. This is the same hazard as component discovery and demands the same defense: a façade self-check (expected-vs-found resource manifest) that fails loudly. Spring's analogous footgun (the candidate-index all-or-nothing, doc line 572) is instructive — leaf must avoid recreating it for resources.
- AFIT/RPITIT not dyn-compatible vs an object-safe `Resource`: the abstraction wants `async fn open()` AND wants `dyn Resource` (so origins are pluggable and the WASM source slots in). On stable these can't both hold on the same surface — the dyn path must box the open future (alloc per open). The design must choose where to pay it: always-boxed (R1/R2, simple, alloc per open) vs a zero-cost typed path with dyn as escape hatch (R3, faster but two-path complexity).
- `AsyncRead`/runtime coupling vs runtime-agnosticism (§2.6): a `Resource` that streams must commit to SOME async-read trait surface (tokio's `AsyncRead`, futures' `AsyncRead`, or a leaf-owned trait). Spring's `getInputStream()` is a trivial sync `InputStream`; the async-first charter forces a streaming abstraction that risks pinning leaf to a runtime's I/O trait — itself a deferred decision the resource trait must avoid prejudging (likely a leaf-owned reader trait or a `Bytes`-slurp default with an optional stream arm).
- `getFile()`/`getURL()` don't always exist: Spring's `Resource` optimistically exposes `getFile()`/`getURL()`/`lastModified()` and throws when an origin can't honor them (a classpath resource inside a jar has no `File`). In Rust this must be modeled as `Option`/typed-capability rather than throwing — an embedded `classpath:` resource has no `Path` and no `Url`, a URL resource has no `Path`, etc. The 'uniform handle' is really a handle with origin-varying capabilities, which Rust's type system surfaces honestly (Option/sub-traits) rather than papering over with exceptions.
- exists()/last_modified() can't always be answered without I/O or at all: for an embedded resource `exists` is a sync O(1) table hit; for a `file:` it needs a stat (I/O — should it be async?); for a URL it may be unknowable without a request. Spring conflates these behind a sync `exists()` that quietly does I/O. leaf must decide whether `exists` is sync-but-maybe-cheap-only, async, or a tri-state `Known/Unknown` — an honest model the JVM hides. (R1 proposes a `ResourceExistence::{Known(bool),Unknown}` to avoid lying.)
- Generic resources can't be link-registered (mirrors the component clash): a typed/monomorphized resource (R3) has no single runtime symbol for link-time collection, so the cross-crate embedded table must stay type-erased entries — the zero-cost typed path and the link-time registry don't fully meet, forcing a typed-view-over-erased-entry seam exactly as the bean registry faces for generic components.

### Interactions
- **container-core** — Resource loading IS one of the context-services the ApplicationContext façade layers over the bare engine (container-core R1/R2/R3 list it explicitly as a façade-exposed capability the bare engine lacks). The loader is constructed during façade bring-up and exposed via the same context-service mechanism container-core chooses for events/messages — and whether it is always-present (R1-style) or an attachable capability (R2/R3-style) is container-core's call, not this feature's.
- **component-scanning** — Primary consumer. component-scanning's enumeration step is Spring's `classpath*:`+pkg+`**/*.class` via the pattern resolver (doc line 523). In leaf this becomes a `resolve_pattern` over the embedded/registered resource table — so resource-loading's pattern resolver IS the substrate component-scanning enumerates over. They share the identical link-time/DCE hazard and almost certainly share the SAME cross-crate registry substrate (a deep unification candidate).
- **config-data** — Primary consumer. config-data loads application/profile files from prefixed locations (`spring.config.import`, `env:`, `configtree:` — doc line 258/1196) which are exactly `ResourceLoader` location strings. R2 makes this a near-fusion (shared `ContentSource` SPI); even R1/R3 require config-data to depend on the resolver and config-data's location-prefix providers to register as resource schemes. The execution-ordering constraint (config loads at environment-prep, before beans) flows back into when the resolver must be usable.
- **condition-family** — Direct consumer via the OnResource condition. Spring's `@ConditionalOnResource` is built on `ConditionContext.getResourceLoader()` (doc line 1121); leaf's condition-family OnResource queries this loader's `exists`/`resolve`. Because conditions are inherently dynamic/runtime, they consume the dyn `ResourceLoader` (R3's dyn path), and the loader must be available during condition evaluation (parse/register phases).
- **origin-tracking** — Deep affinity, strongest in R2. Every `Resource`/`ContentSource` carries an `Origin` (file/line/owning-source) which is precisely origin-tracking's currency. R2 makes provenance mandatory on the shared SPI so config values and resources share one provenance type; R1/R3 still must thread a `ResourceId`/origin through `ResourceError` for §2.9 diagnostics. Resource-loading is a major SOURCE of the origins origin-tracking propagates.
- **property-sources** — Adjacent and unification-candidate (the crux of R2). A property source is a parsed view over loaded bytes from a named origin — nearly a `Resource` plus a parser. R2 proposes one shared `ContentSource` substrate for both; R1/R3 keep them separate but property-sources still obtains its raw bytes by resolving resources. The seam (shared content layer vs resource-only pattern/stream layer) is a key cross-cutting question.
- **messages-i18n** — Consumer. MessageSource resolves localized bundles from basename locations (the leaf analogue of Spring's resource-bundle loading), which are `ResourceLoader` locations resolved per-locale. messages-i18n depends on the loader to open the correct bundle resource; like resource-loading it is a façade-only context service, so they appear together on the context surface.
- **aware-callbacks** — Injection seam. Spring fires `ResourceLoaderAware` as part of the context-aware group (doc line 894/2494) and the loader sits in resolvableDependencies (line 705). leaf's aware-callbacks / resolvableDependency mechanism is how infrastructure beans receive `Arc<dyn ResourcePatternResolver>` — resource-loading defines the injectable handle, aware-callbacks defines the delivery.
- **environment** — Bidirectional. Locations carry `${...}` placeholders (doc line 522: base packages accept placeholders) resolved against the Environment, so the loader may need environment-backed placeholder resolution at resolve time; conversely config-data uses the loader to BUILD the environment. An ordering/dependency tension (which exists first) that container-core's bring-up order must sequence.
- **type-conversion** — Light consumer. value-injection/binding may convert a `${property}` location string into a `Resource` (Spring registers a `ResourceEditor`/`ResourceEditorRegistrar`, doc line 355) — i.e. 'inject a Resource from a location string property' is a conversion from `Location`→`Resource` that type-conversion's registry would carry, delegating the actual resolve to this loader.
- **auto-configuration** — Consumer. Auto-config candidates are discovered from a `*.imports`-equivalent resource read across all contributors (doc line 1196: `getResources` across jars). In leaf this is another `classpath*:`/registered-table enumeration over the resource substrate — so auto-configuration's discovery rides resource-loading's pattern resolver and inherits its Layer-0/self-check requirements.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Is `classpath:` a SEPARATE resource registry, or does it share ONE cross-crate substrate (and even one collected table) with component-scanning and auto-configuration discovery? All three are `classpath*:`-shaped enumeration over linked contributors with the identical Layer-0/DCE hazard — unifying them (one registry, one self-check, one substrate) vs keeping bespoke registries is a §2.11 unification call that needs the whole catalog to judge.
- Does resource-loading FUSE with property-sources/config-data/origin-tracking on a shared `ContentSource`+`Origin` primitive (R2), or stay a separate ResourceLoader that those features merely consume (R1/R3)? This trades maximal unification and free provenance against coupling and the large-resource-vs-small-config impedance mismatch — a genuine meta-architecture question, not resolvable per-feature.
- What is the async-read / streaming trait surface for `Resource::open`, given runtime-agnosticism (§2.6)? Commit to tokio `AsyncRead`, futures `AsyncRead`, a leaf-owned reader trait, or default to a `Bytes` slurp with an optional stream arm? This is part of the deferred async-execution-model decision and the resource trait must not prejudge it.
- Always-boxed `dyn Resource`/boxed-open-future (R1/R2, simple, alloc per open) vs a zero-cost monomorphized typed path with `dyn` as escape hatch (R3, faster, two-path complexity)? This is the same async-across-dyn boxing tradeoff container-core flagged, instantiated for resources, and is the §3 async-execution-model decision.
- What is the cross-crate substrate (A linkme / B+force-link / C build.rs codegen / D explicit) for collecting embedded `classpath:` `ResourceEntry` descriptors, and how does the mandatory anti-silent-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found resource manifest) bind to it? Resource-loading is substrate-neutral by design but the façade's self-check behavior must bind to whichever substrate Phase 2 picks — and ideally the SAME one components use.
- How is the static-vs-dynamic resource-source DUALITY exposed: the link-time embedded table as the default 'classpath' PLUS an optional dynamic directory-scanned source (config dir) PLUS a future WASM-module resource table — as multiple registered providers feeding one resolver (candidate), and is enabling a dynamic source explicit/scoped (predictability concern from the cross-crate doc) or implicit/global?
- How honest must `exists()`/`last_modified()` be about origin-varying capability and I/O cost — a sync best-effort bool (Spring's lie), an async method, or a tri-state `Known/Unknown`? And should `getFile()`/`getUrl()` be `Option`/sub-trait capabilities rather than always-present-but-may-fail? Touches the diagnostics model (§2.9) and the type-erasure/handle substrate.
- Can statically-named resources (`#[resource("banner.txt")]`, fixed config locations) have their MISSING-resource error hoisted to compile/codegen time (R3) per §2.9's richest-diagnostic-timing preference, and how does that interact with the conditional strategy (cfg vs codegen vs runtime) — i.e. is a resource's presence a build-time-frozen fact or a runtime gate?
- Where do `${...}` placeholder-bearing locations get resolved (loader-side vs caller-side), given the chicken-and-egg with environment (config-data uses the loader to build the environment, but locations may reference environment properties)? This ordering constraint is cross-cutting with environment, config-data, and container-core's bring-up sequence.

### Notes
Confidence: high on intent — the Spring section is explicit that resource loading is a context-service of the ApplicationContext façade (lines 49/112/128), consumed by scanning (523), config/imports (258/1196), and conditions (1121), and injected via the aware/resolvableDependencies seam (705/894/2494). I read all of those plus the scanning mechanics and condition-context sections in full.

The three realizations are genuinely divergent on the axis that matters for THIS feature — NOT 'which cross-crate substrate' (that is a separate, cross-cutting Phase 2 decision I deliberately kept all three neutral on), but rather WHAT THE RESOURCE ABSTRACTION IS:
- R1: a faithful async port of Spring's three-trait shape (Resource / ResourceLoader / ResourcePatternResolver) with `classpath:` re-realized as a synthetic embedded entry-table — closest intent parity, always-dyn, simplest.
- R2: resources as a UNIFICATION with property-sources/config-data/origin-tracking via one `ContentSource`+`Origin` primitive — maximal §2.11 unification and free provenance, at the cost of coupling and the big-resource-vs-small-config mismatch; explicitly flagged as a candidate that borders on meta-architecture.
- R3: a zero-cost monomorphized typed path (known locations resolved at compile/codegen time) with `dyn` reserved as the dynamic/WASM escape hatch — best low-overhead and even compile-time miss-detection for same-crate statics, at the cost of two-path complexity and divergence from Spring's single-loader model.

Three things to carry forward: (1) The single most consequential rust-native fact is that `classpath:` has no JVM analogue — it MUST become a closed, build/link-time-collected embedded namespace, which makes `classpath*:` enumeration actually possible (finite table) but drags in the FULL Layer-0/DCE silent-miss hazard, now for resources; a façade self-check (expected-vs-found resource manifest) is non-negotiable in every realization. (2) This feature is almost certainly the SAME enumeration substrate as component-scanning and auto-config discovery — I treated 'do they share one registry' as a top phase2Question rather than deciding it, because it is a §2.11 unification call. (3) Two clashes dominate downstream and belong to Phase 2: the async-read/streaming trait surface (runtime-agnosticism §2.6) and the always-boxed-vs-typed-path tradeoff — I refused to settle either; both appear as phase2Questions.

I kept the provider/registry abstraction strictly origin-agnostic across all three (consumers see `dyn Resource`/`ContentSource`; a WASM-module resource source is just another registered provider/table) per the brief's hard constraint, and I surfaced the static-embedded + dynamic-directory + future-wasm DUALITY as multiple providers feeding one resolver — a candidate, not a decision (most natural in R2 because config-data's multi-prefix location model already wants exactly that shape).

Naming ('Resource', 'ResourceLoader', 'ResourcePatternResolver', 'ContentSource', 'ResourceEntry', 'Location'/'Pattern'/'Scheme') is Phase-1 placeholder. I wrote no files. Grounding paths (all absolute): /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/spring-boot-4-di-design.md (lines 49/112/128 façade-service framing, 303 banner.location, 355 ResourceEditorRegistrar/resolvableDependencies, 518-555 scanning+resourcePattern mechanics, 705 resolvableDependencies, 894/2494 ResourceLoaderAware ordering, 1121 ConditionContext.getResourceLoader, 1196 *.imports getResources-across-jars), /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-14-leaf-charter-design.md (invariants §2, deferred §3), /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/rust-cross-crate-composition.md (Layer-0/A/B DCE, Architectures A-D, scope-don't-globalize, mandatory self-check), /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/rust-nightly-features-tradeoffs.md (RPITIT/AFIT not dyn-compatible → boxed futures at dyn boundary, trait upcasting 1.86, Arc<dyn Any>/TypeId registry, no async Drop, async-read on stable).

## Context Propagation (holder/strategy + SPI)  `[context-propagation]`

Spring's "ambient context" — the current request (RequestContextHolder), locale (LocaleContextHolder), and transaction resources (TransactionSynchronizationManager) — lives in ThreadLocal, which works only while a logical unit of work stays pinned to ONE thread and silently breaks at every thread hop the TaskExecutor abstraction introduces (spring doc 2089-2095). The holder/strategy pattern (a static-method facade as API contract over a hidden ThreadLocal storage strategy, with NamedThreadLocal so leaks are heap-dump-identifiable, a dual plain/inheritable field with inheritable OFF by default, and transaction resources NEVER inheritable for correctness) is per-concern; before the SPI, every concern (tracing, MDC, security, locale, tenant) reinvented its own "copy my ThreadLocal to the other thread" code and none composed (2120-2122). The `io.micrometer:context-propagation` SPI GENERALIZES the holder pattern into FOUR neutral abstractions: ThreadLocalAccessor<V> (key()/getValue()/setValue(V)/no-arg setValue() to clear/restore(prev)/no-arg restore() — entry/exit pair replacing deprecated reset()); ContextAccessor (the map-like dual for Reactor Context); a ContextRegistry of accessors (ServiceLoader-discovered, so jars-on-classpath makes propagation 'just work'); and ContextSnapshot (immutable captured values keyed by key()). THE CAPTURE/RESTORE LIFECYCLE is the load-bearing intent: captureAll() iterates every registered accessor calling getValue(), storing non-null values into an immutable snapshot; on the borrowing execution context setThreadLocals() returns an AutoCloseable Scope that on open calls setValue(captured) and CRITICALLY saves the target's CURRENT getValue() as previousValue, and on close calls restore(previousValue) — restore-not-clear, because a borrowed/pooled worker can't be assumed empty, so blind clearing would cross-contaminate (2129-2135). The whole point: one captureAll()/setThreadLocals() moves ALL registered contexts atomically across ANY boundary (ThreadLocal, Reactor Context, coroutine) — adapt only at the seams, never force a rewrite of imperative-vs-reactive code. Wired into execution via ContextPropagatingTaskDecorator (captures at submit on the caller, opens Scope before run, closes after) — and Spring keeps it OPT-IN by default (Boot 4 spring.task.execution.propagate-context=false) because implicit propagation into every async task risks stale-tenant/security data bleed and costs CPU per task; magic traded for predictability (2149-2155). leaf must realize this INTENT: a composable, neutral, multi-source capture/restore SPI that survives async thread hops, opt-in, leak-free, origin-agnostic — NOT the ThreadLocal mechanism, which is actively wrong across an .await (a task migrates threads under work-stealing, so the value belongs to the logical task, not the OS thread). This feature defines WHAT is captured/restored and the composition of multiple sources; it does NOT define the holders themselves (that is locale-context) nor the executor/decorator-chain plumbing (that is task-execution) — it is the keystone the charter §3 explicitly defers ('the rust-native answer to ThreadLocal holders across .await').

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Micrometer-faithful port: runtime registry of type-erased ContextAccessors + immutable ContextSnapshot + RAII restore-Scope, captured/restored explicitly at task boundaries
The most literal intent-port of the Micrometer SPI, re-pointed off ThreadLocal onto a task-scoped store. THREE neutral abstractions mirror the four Micrometer ones: (1) `trait ContextAccessor: Send + Sync { fn key(&self) -> ContextKey; fn capture(&self) -> Option<CapturedValue>; fn restore_into(&self, v: CapturedValue) -> RestoreGuard; }` where CapturedValue is a type-erased `Box<dyn Any + Send>` (or an Arc for cheap clone) keyed by a stable ContextKey (a &'static str newtype, the NamedThreadLocal name re-purposed as the registry key) — this is the ThreadLocalAccessor analogue, but `restore_into` returns an RAII guard whose Drop restores the previous value (the try-with-resources Scope, made Rust-native via Drop rather than a close() call, since restore is purely synchronous and non-blocking so Drop is safe here — unlike async shutdown). (2) `ContextRegistry` — an injectable, container-owned bean (NOT a global static; charter 'scope discovery, don't make it implicitly global') holding `Vec<Arc<dyn ContextAccessor>>`; accessors are CONTRIBUTED by integration crates (a tracing accessor in leaf-observability, a locale accessor from locale-context) via the same descriptor substrate every other contribution uses — registered as data, ordered/keyed at runtime. (3) `ContextSnapshot` — an immutable `Arc<[(ContextKey, CapturedValue)]>` produced by `registry.capture_all()` which iterates accessors calling capture(), storing only Some values. RESTORE LIFECYCLE: `snapshot.restore()` returns a `RestoreScope` holding the per-accessor RestoreGuards; on construction each accessor saves the target's CURRENT value as previous and installs the captured one; on RestoreScope Drop the guards restore previous in reverse (restore-not-clear contamination defense). Where the ambient value physically LIVES is the locale-context concern (a task-local, an Arc-cell in the request scope, etc.); this feature only sees it through the accessor's capture/restore. Propagation across a hop is EXPLICIT and opt-in: the TaskDecorator seam task-execution exposes is implemented here as a `ContextPropagatingDecorator { snapshot_fn }` that at submit-time calls registry.capture_all() on the caller's task, moves the (Send) snapshot into the spawned future, and on first poll opens snapshot.restore() (held for the future's lifetime, dropped on completion). Off by default; enabled per-executor/per-profile (the spring.task.execution.propagate-context analogue).

**Pros:** Tightest intent parity with Micrometer: capture_all / restore / RAII-Scope / restore-not-clear / multi-source registry port 1:1, so the Spring mental model (and its documentation) transfers, and the 'add an accessor, all boundaries carry it' composability is preserved exactly.; Origin-agnostic and pluggable by construction: accessors are dyn-trait beans contributed cross-crate; a WASM-module layer, a tracing crate, or a test double all register accessors identically — the registry never assumes where a context value is constructed or stored (charter provider-of-dyn-Trait neutrality).; RAII RestoreScope is a genuine Rust WIN over the JVM try-with-resources idiom: leak-free borrowing is enforced by the borrow checker / Drop, not by developer discipline — a mismatched open/close (the classic Micrometer 'scope leak' warning, 2147) becomes structurally impossible.; Restore-not-clear is the SAME contamination defense Spring needs but here it defends against a reused async worker / pooled task slot rather than a pooled thread — directly serves charter abuse-resistance against stale-tenant data bleed.; Decouples cleanly from locale-context (which owns the holders) and task-execution (which owns the decorator chain): this feature is purely the neutral capture/restore vocabulary, maximizing unification (one SPI, every concern).

**Cons:** Type-erasure tax: every captured value is Box<dyn Any + Send> keyed by a runtime ContextKey, so capture_all walks a Vec and boxes per source per submission — fine on cold/coarse async hops (scheduled jobs, async-event dispatch) but a per-task alloc + dyn-call on hot per-request fan-out (charter low-overhead §2 tension); the zero-cost typed path is lost at the erased SPI boundary.; 'Where the value lives' is deliberately left to the accessor, so this realization does NOT by itself answer the deepest clash — if an accessor is naively backed by a real thread_local!, it is WRONG across an .await (the value won't follow a work-stealing task migration). The SPI is only correct if accessors are backed by a task-scoped store; this realization DECLARES the seam but pushes the hard correctness question onto locale-context's holder mechanism (a phase2Question).; Restore-on-first-poll vs restore-for-whole-future is subtle: a future that yields at an .await and resumes on a DIFFERENT worker must re-install the snapshot on each resume, not just first poll — meaning the RestoreScope cannot simply live across awaits as a plain guard; it must be re-entered at every poll, which a naive Drop-guard does not do (this is exactly the ThreadContextElement problem and pushes toward R2's poll-wrapping for correctness).; ContextKey-as-string is stringly-typed: a typo or a duplicate key across two crates is a runtime/startup error, not a compile error (charter prefers earliest legible diagnostic) — needs a startup validation pass over the registry for duplicate/missing keys.; capture_all is unconditional over ALL registered accessors; predicate-filtered capture (Micrometer's ContextSnapshotFactory) and per-key opt-in must be added or every hop pays for every registered concern.

**Mechanisms considered:** runtime registry (injectable ContextRegistry bean) of Arc<dyn ContextAccessor> — runtime collection, NOT a global static (scoped discovery); cross-crate accessor contribution via the shared descriptor substrate (linkme distributed-slice default / inventory for runtime-computed / explicit builder) — same Layer-0 force-link + self-check obligations as any contribution; type-erased CapturedValue = Box<dyn Any + Send> keyed by const ContextKey (&'static str newtype); Any+downcast (stable) as the storage backbone; RAII RestoreScope holding per-accessor guards whose Drop restores previous value (try-with-resources Scope -> Rust Drop, sync-only so Drop is safe); ContextPropagatingDecorator implementing task-execution's TaskDecorator seam — capture at submit, move snapshot into spawned future, restore on poll; opt-in per executor/profile; accessor backing store left abstract (task-local / request-scope Arc-cell / module store) — the holder mechanism is locale-context's, deferred

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The ContextAccessor trait, ContextKey, ContextSnapshot, ContextRegistry, and the ContextPropagatingDecorator live in leaf-core (naming no runtime, no concrete holder). Accessors are CONTRIBUTED by sibling/integration crates (locale accessor, a tracing/observation accessor in leaf-observability, a tenant accessor in an app crate) — this is the classic Spring ServiceLoader-of-accessors story (Micrometer discovers accessors via META-INF/services, 2126/2139) and maps onto leaf's cross-crate substrate exactly: each accessor is a thin const/runtime descriptor registered via linkme (default) / inventory (if the accessor needs runtime-computed setup) / explicit builder, and is subject to Layer-0 DCE — a declared-but-unreferenced accessor crate silently contributes NOTHING, yielding an empty registry and SILENTLY-DROPPED context (a subtle correctness bug: propagation just stops carrying that concern, no error). Mitigation candidates (deferred): the same force-link + startup self-check the composition doc mandates, here listing 'discovered accessors: [tracing, locale, ...]' so a missing one is loud (charter rich diagnostics). Crucially, unlike task-execution's executor, a MISSING accessor is degraded-not-fatal (context for that concern simply doesn't propagate), so the self-check is a WARNING surface rather than a hard refresh failure — but Micrometer's 'jars-on-classpath makes propagation just work' magic (which 'can baffle anyone debugging why context moves', 2139) is a DX hazard leaf should counter by making the accessor set INSPECTABLE (list registered accessors + their keys at startup). Ordering of accessors is resolved at runtime by a priority field, never link order. Origin-agnostic: a WASM-module-backed accessor (capturing context inside a guest) registers via the same SPI.

**T2 — execution context:** capture_all() runs SYNCHRONOUSLY on the CALLER's task at submit time (cheap: a Vec walk + per-accessor capture(), each a getValue()-style read + box) — must NOT block (accessors read ambient state, never do IO). The produced ContextSnapshot must be Send so it can move into the spawned future (a hard bound: any captured value must be Send + 'static, which fractures vs Spring where any object is captured — a non-Send ambient value cannot cross a task hop at all). restore() runs on the BORROWING task: it installs captured values into whatever task-scoped store the accessor uses, saving previous for restore. The cancellation/leak contract: because restore is sync, the RestoreScope guard's Drop restores cleanly even if the spawned future is CANCELLED mid-flight (dropped at an await) — RAII guarantees no contaminated leftover in the borrowed slot, a Rust-native win over JVM (no try-finally needed; cancellation can't skip the restore). THE HARD T2 PROBLEM: a future can migrate workers at every .await under work-stealing, so a one-shot 'restore before run, drop after' is INSUFFICIENT for value-based accessors that read a real thread-local — correctness requires the snapshot be re-installed on EACH poll resumption (the ThreadContextElement/PropagationContextElement intent, 2159). This realization is fully correct only when accessors are backed by a TASK-scoped store (the value rides the task, no per-poll reinstall needed) — if backed by a thread-local, it needs R2's poll-wrapping. Errors: capture/restore are infallible by contract (an accessor that can't read returns None / restores nothing); a panicking accessor must be isolated (caught at the seam) so one bad context source can't poison the whole hop. Scope-based accessors (the ObservationThreadLocalAccessor analogue, where setValue opens a scope and no-value opens a NullObservation MASK rather than clearing, 2147) are expressible: such an accessor's restore_into pushes a scope and its guard pops it — but the open/close balance is now Drop-enforced, removing the classic leak. No global lock; the registry is read-only after refresh, snapshots are immutable Arc, the only per-task state is the moved snapshot + guards (stack/Arc, minimal heap).

#### R2 — Context rides the future: a poll-wrapping combinator over an injectable Context bundle (the ThreadContextElement-analogue, structured to survive every .await)
Attack the deepest clash head-on: in async Rust the unit that hops threads is the FUTURE (it can migrate workers at any await), so context must be PINNED TO THE FUTURE, re-established on every poll, not captured-once at spawn. Model an ambient Context as a single opaque bundle `Context` (an immutable, cheaply-clonable Arc-backed map from ContextKey to Arc<dyn Any + Send + Sync>, composed from the SAME ContextAccessor contributions as R1 — R2 reuses R1's accessor SPI for the capture side). The propagation primitive is a future combinator: `fut.with_context(ctx)` returns a `WithContext<F>` whose `poll` (a) installs ctx into a single framework-owned task-local (`tokio::task_local!`-style, or a stable std task-local shim) for the duration of THIS poll, (b) polls the inner future, (c) restores the prior task-local value on the way out — every poll, so a resume on any worker re-establishes the context. This is the literal Rust analogue of Kotlin's ThreadContextElement / Framework 7's PropagationContextElement (2159): the context is a property of the suspendable computation, re-applied at each resumption. 'The current X' lookups (locale-context's job) read from the framework task-local, which is ALWAYS correct because WithContext guarantees it is installed whenever the wrapped future is running, regardless of which worker polls it. Propagation across a spawn is then trivial and STRUCTURED: capture the current Context (a single Arc clone, no per-accessor box), and spawn `spawned_fut.with_context(captured)` — the child future carries the parent's context by value, surviving arbitrary work-stealing. Accessors are still the contribution/extensibility seam (each accessor knows how to lift its concern's value INTO and read it OUT OF the Context bundle), but the cross-boundary movement is one Arc clone + a poll-wrapper, not a Vec-of-boxes restore dance. Opt-in stays: an un-wrapped spawned future simply has no context (isolated by default).

**Pros:** CORRECT across every .await by construction — re-installing on each poll is the only model that survives work-stealing task migration, directly solving the clash R1 only declares; 'the current locale/request' is guaranteed live whenever the wrapped future runs (charter §2.3 explicit-execution-context, made airtight).; Cheap cross-boundary movement: propagation is ONE Arc clone of the immutable Context bundle (structural sharing) plus a zero-alloc poll-wrapper — no per-accessor box per hop, far better on hot per-request fan-out than R1's capture_all (charter low-overhead §2).; Structured-concurrency-friendly: because context rides the future as a value, a child task's context is lexically the parent's at spawn — composes with scoped-task patterns and makes 'this work runs under this request/tenant' a property of the future tree, not a fragile side-channel that can desync.; Single framework task-local (one well-known name) instead of N per-concern thread-locals: locale-context's holders all read one bundle, so there is exactly ONE place context can leak and ONE place to inspect — far better debuggability than Micrometer's N ServiceLoader-discovered accessors silently moving values (counters the 'baffling why context moves' hazard, 2139).; Reactive-on-hot-paths aligned (charter §2.4): poll-wrapping is event-driven (it acts exactly when the runtime polls), never busy-waits; the wrapper is a thin Future adapter with no timer/loop.

**Cons:** Requires a task-local primitive: tokio's task_local! is runtime-specific (clashes with charter §2.6 runtime-agnosticism — the core must not name tokio); a stable std task-local-across-await does NOT exist (std thread_local is wrong; std has no ScopedValue-async), so leaf must ship its own task-local-via-poll-wrapper abstraction in core and have the runtime integration provide the storage — a real design burden and the crux phase2Question.; Per-poll install/restore has a (small) cost on EVERY poll of a wrapped future, not just at hops — for a future that awaits thousands of times this is thousands of task-local swaps; cheaper than R1's per-hop box but paid more often. Needs measurement; may want to skip the swap when ctx is unchanged.; Opaque single-bundle Context loses Micrometer's per-accessor restore-not-clear nuance and scope-based accessors (ObservationThreadLocalAccessor's openScope/NullObservation masking, 2147): a scope-stack concern doesn't map cleanly onto a value-map bundle and may need a side mechanism, so full parity with scope-based contexts is harder than R1.; All context values must be Send + Sync + 'static (Arc<dyn Any + Send + Sync>) to ride a multi-worker future — even stricter than R1's Send-only, excluding !Sync ambient values entirely; a genuine narrowing vs Spring's 'any object'.; Less of a literal Micrometer port — practitioners expecting capture_all()/setThreadLocals()/Scope must learn 'wrap the future' instead; the SPI shape diverges (intent-parity says acceptable, but it's teaching friction and the accessor SPI now serves only capture-into-bundle, not restore).

**Mechanisms considered:** future combinator `WithContext<F>` re-installing context on EVERY poll (ThreadContextElement / kotlinx PropagationContextElement analogue, 2159) — the structured-across-await mechanism; single immutable Arc-backed Context bundle (ContextKey -> Arc<dyn Any + Send + Sync>) as the propagated value; structural-sharing clone on hop; one framework-owned task-local for 'the current context'; storage provided by the runtime integration crate (core defines the trait, leaf-tokio backs it with tokio::task_local!); ContextAccessor SPI (reused from R1) for the capture/lift side only — each concern knows how to put/read its value in the bundle; opt-in by spawning future.with_context(ctx); un-wrapped futures isolated (data-bleed default-off); optional skip-swap-when-unchanged optimization to amortize per-poll cost

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The Context bundle type, the WithContext combinator, the framework task-local TRAIT, and the (reused) ContextAccessor SPI live in leaf-core; the task-local STORAGE backing is runtime-coupled and lives in the integration crate (leaf-tokio uses tokio::task_local!; a smol/other integration provides its own) — same mandatory-runtime Layer-0 hazard as task-execution: if the runtime crate that provides the task-local storage isn't force-linked, context propagation has no backing store. But unlike task-execution's executor this is degraded-not-fatal at the propagation layer (no storage -> no propagation), so the self-check is a warning. Accessors that LIFT concern values into the bundle are cross-crate contributions via the shared descriptor substrate (linkme/inventory/explicit), subject to the same DCE/force-link discipline as R1 — a missing accessor means that concern silently isn't captured. The big T1 nuance: because there is ONE task-local and ONE bundle, the per-concern accessor set is smaller and the 'which concerns propagate' surface is a single inspectable bundle schema rather than N independently-discovered accessors — easier to validate at startup. Origin-agnostic: a WASM module that needs the ambient context receives the bundle marshalled across the boundary (the proxy reads the task-local at the call seam and lowers it into the WIT call); the bundle's Any-keyed values are the marshalling unit.

**T2 — execution context:** This realization IS the rust-native answer to the clash. WithContext::poll installs the bundle into the framework task-local, polls inner, restores prior — ON EVERY POLL, so context is correct no matter which worker resumes the future after an .await migration (the work-stealing-migration problem solved structurally). Install/restore are sync, non-blocking, infallible. CANCELLATION: if the wrapped future is dropped mid-flight (cancelled at an await), the task-local was only installed during a poll and restored at poll-exit, so there is NOTHING to leak — the borrowed slot is pristine between polls by construction (a cleaner cancellation story than R1's cross-await guard). Propagation at a SPAWN: capture = one Arc clone of the current bundle (read from the task-local) on the caller's task; the child is spawned as child_fut.with_context(captured_bundle) — the child carries the parent context by value across the task hop, and because it re-installs per poll it stays correct through the child's own awaits and migrations. ERRORS: a fire-and-forget spawned task that needs context but was spawned un-wrapped simply sees no context (default isolation) — never a panic; an accessor lifting a value into the bundle that fails returns nothing for its key. Send/Sync bounds: the bundle is Arc<...Send + Sync + 'static>, mandatory because the future runs on multi-worker runtimes — a !Send/!Sync ambient value cannot be propagated and that is a compile-time-visible constraint (charter explicit execution context). Transaction-resource context (the TransactionSynchronizationManager analogue, which Spring makes NEVER inheritable for correctness, 2114-2118): such a concern should DELIBERATELY NOT be auto-propagated — modeled as a context value the propagation policy excludes by default (a connection/transaction must not silently ride to a child task and shatter isolation), the rust-native form of 'never inheritable'. No global lock; the task-local is per-task, the bundle is immutable Arc (structural sharing), no shared-mutable state.

#### R3 — Context as an explicit injectable value (no ambient side-channel): a typed Context handle threaded through the call graph, with an opt-in ambient bridge only at framework seams
Question whether leaf should reproduce the ambient/holder pattern AT ALL on hot paths. Spring's holder exists to avoid 'threading a RequestContext through every method signature' (viral, intrusive — 2112); but Rust's async model already threads state explicitly all the time, and the charter prizes explicit execution context (§2.3) over magic. So make the PRIMARY model an explicit, injectable `Context` value — a cheaply-clonable immutable handle (Arc-backed typed map, same bundle as R2) that beans RECEIVE as a normal injected/passed parameter (`async fn handle(&self, cx: &Context)`), and read typed slices from via `cx.get::<Locale>()` / `cx.with(tenant)`. Propagation across a task hop is then NOT a hidden capture/restore at all — it is ordinary value passing: you clone the Context (Arc bump) and pass it to the spawned future, exactly as you pass any other argument. This makes 'what context this work runs under' VISIBLE in signatures and impossible to silently lose (no DCE'd accessor, no thread-local-vs-task-local footgun, no per-poll swap). The capture/restore SPI is NOT eliminated but DEMOTED to a compatibility bridge: at the boundaries where leaf integrates with code that genuinely needs ambient lookup (legacy-style holders, a tracing crate that reads a thread-local, a WASM guest, framework interception points where threading a param is impossible), an explicit `cx.enter()` opens a scope (the R2 poll-wrapper / R1 RAII-Scope, reused) that publishes the explicit Context into the ambient task-local for the duration — so ambient lookup is an OPT-IN PROJECTION of the explicit value, never the source of truth. The ContextAccessor SPI survives as the adapter set for these bridges (lift a Context slice into a tracing scope, etc.). This inverts Spring: explicit-by-default, ambient-by-exception, with the holder/strategy capture/restore retained ONLY as the seam adapter.

**Pros:** Maximally honest and abuse-resistant (charter §2.3): 'this work runs under this request/locale/tenant' is in the type signature, not a hidden side-channel — context CANNOT be silently lost (no empty-registry DCE bug, no thread-local-across-await footgun) and CANNOT silently bleed (a child only has context you explicitly passed it), eliminating both the data-bleed and the 'baffling why context moves' hazards at the root.; Zero ambient machinery on the hot path: passing &Context is a borrow/Arc-clone, no task-local install/restore per poll (R2's cost) and no capture_all box-dance per hop (R1's cost) — the cheapest steady-state model, best aligns with low-overhead #2 when context is on the explicit path.; The capture/restore SPI shrinks to exactly where it is unavoidable (interception seams, legacy/tracing bridges, WASM guests) — so the holder pattern's complexity (restore-not-clear, scope masking, per-poll reinstall) is paid only at those few seams, not framework-wide; smaller correctness surface.; Transaction-resource 'never inheritable' (2114-2118) becomes the DEFAULT, not a special case: a transaction handle simply isn't in the Context you pass to a child unless you explicitly put it there — correctness-by-omission.; Most rust-native and most unifying with dependency injection: Context is just another injectable, so deferral-primitives / scopes / autowiring all apply; 'the current request scope' (scopes/scoped-proxies neighbours) is naturally the Context value bound to that scope.

**Cons:** Largest DIVERGENCE from Spring intent: Spring's WHOLE point is ambient 'current X' WITHOUT threading a parameter (2112); making explicit-passing primary rejects the holder ergonomics that define this feature — a real intent-parity tension (charter §2.2 says realize intent, but here the intent IS ambient access; this realization argues the JVM forced ambient because explicit threading was viral, and Rust's async signatures already thread state, so the intent may not survive translation — a claim Phase 2/3 must judge).; Viral signatures: &Context (or cx: Context) must appear on every method that needs it AND every method that merely passes it through to something that needs it — exactly the 'pollutes APIs and couples unrelated layers' problem Spring's holder was invented to AVOID (2112). On a deep call graph this is heavy ceremony, hurting DX #1.; Interception/AOP seams (transaction, cache, retry, async-execution proxies — the entire AOP cluster) CANNOT thread a param through user code they wrap, so they MUST use the ambient bridge — meaning the 'demoted' capture/restore path is actually load-bearing for the most important cross-cutting features, so R3 doesn't escape R1/R2's hard problems, it just relocates them to the AOP boundary (and now has TWO models — explicit + ambient — to keep coherent).; Two coexisting models (explicit value + ambient bridge) is a unification COST, not a win: developers must know which is in play where, and a value read explicitly vs via ambient projection can DESYNC if the bridge scope is mis-nested — a new failure mode neither R1 nor R2 has.; Async-event dispatch, scheduling, and background-bootstrap (which invoke user code with no natural place to pass a Context) all fall back to the ambient bridge, so the 'explicit-primary' benefit evaporates for precisely the thread-hopping cases this feature exists to serve.

**Mechanisms considered:** explicit injectable immutable Context handle (Arc-backed typed map) passed/injected as a normal value — propagation = ordinary value passing (Arc clone); typed accessors cx.get::<T>() over the bundle (downcast on Any), composable cx.with(value) returning a derived child context; ambient bridge cx.enter() reusing R2's poll-wrapper (or R1's RAII Scope) to PROJECT the explicit value into a framework task-local at seams only; ContextAccessor SPI demoted to seam-adapters (lift Context slice into tracing scope / WASM marshalling / legacy holder); DI integration: Context is an injectable bean scoped to request/task; scopes + scoped-proxies neighbours supply the per-scope binding; transaction/connection context excluded-by-default (not in the passed Context unless explicit) — 'never inheritable' as the default

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The Context type, typed accessors, and the cx.enter() ambient-bridge live in leaf-core; the bridge's task-local storage is runtime-coupled (same as R2, lives in the integration crate, same mandatory-runtime Layer-0 hazard for the bridge path only). The big T1 advantage: the EXPLICIT path needs NO cross-crate registration at all — Context is a plain value passed through code, so there is no accessor-discovery, no DCE hazard, no force-link obligation for the common case (a genuine reliability win — context can't silently vanish because there's no link-time collection to drop). Cross-crate contribution shrinks to the seam-adapters (tracing bridge, WASM marshalling) registered via the shared substrate, subject to DCE only there. Origin-agnostic: a WASM module receives the Context as an explicit marshalled argument at the call boundary (cleanest of the three — the proxy lowers the passed Context into the WIT call directly, no ambient read needed). The cost moved to T1 elsewhere: because explicit Context is injected, it couples to the scope/registry substrate (charter §3 deferred) — 'how is the request-scoped Context bound and resolved' is a scopes-neighbour question.

**T2 — execution context:** On the explicit path there is NO ambient install/restore and NO per-poll swap: context is a value the future already owns (passed at spawn as child_fut where the closure captured cx.clone()), so it is trivially correct across any .await and any worker migration — the future literally holds its context, nothing to re-establish (the simplest possible T2). CANCELLATION: dropping the future drops its Context (an Arc decrement) — no leak, no contaminated slot, nothing to restore (cleanest cancellation of the three). The ambient-bridge path (cx.enter() at seams) inherits R2's per-poll-reinstall semantics and cancellation cleanliness for exactly the wrapped region — but only that region, so the costly/subtle behavior is bounded to AOP/legacy seams. ERRORS: an explicit Context is infallibly readable (cx.get::<T>() returns Option); a missing expected slice is a typed None the consumer handles, surfaced with rich context (which keys were present) per charter §2.9. Send/Sync: the explicit Context is Arc<...Send + Sync + 'static> so it can be captured into a spawned future — same bound as R2, but here it's the bound on a NORMAL value the developer already sees, not a hidden propagation constraint. Transaction-resource context: excluded by default (not passed to children) — 'never inheritable' realized as the absence of an explicit edge. The hazard: the bridge and the explicit value can DESYNC if a seam projects a stale Context (the bridge scope out-of-sync with the value the next layer reads) — a T2 coherence obligation unique to R3. No global lock; explicit path is pure value passing, bridge path is per-task task-local, both heap-minimal (Arc only).

### Rust clashes
- ThreadLocal is ACTIVELY WRONG across an .await, not merely 'breaks at thread hops' as in Spring. Spring's holder breaks only when work is HANDED to another thread (an explicit TaskExecutor submit); a Rust async task can silently MIGRATE workers at EVERY .await under a work-stealing runtime while it is the 'same' logical task. So std::thread_local read after an await may return a DIFFERENT worker's value with no hop the developer initiated. The correct unit of ambient context is the LOGICAL TASK (the future), not the OS thread — making the entire ThreadLocal storage strategy (the hidden mechanism behind every Spring holder, 2095) the one thing leaf must NOT port. This is the keystone clash the charter §3 explicitly defers.
- No std task-local-across-await primitive on stable. Spring rides ThreadLocal (and Java 21 ScopedValue, the structurally-safe successor it's moving toward, 2164). Rust std has thread_local! (wrong here) and NO async-aware ScopedValue / task-local. tokio::task_local! exists but is runtime-specific — naming it in core violates charter §2.6 runtime-agnosticism. So leaf must DEFINE a task-local/scoped-context abstraction in core (a poll-wrapping combinator) and have the runtime integration crate back its storage — a primitive leaf must build, not import.
- Capture-once-at-submit is insufficient; context must be re-established on EVERY poll. Spring's ContextPropagatingTaskDecorator captures at submit and opens one Scope before run / closes after (2151) — correct because a JVM pooled thread runs the Runnable start-to-finish on one thread. A Rust future resumes on potentially different workers across its awaits, so a one-shot restore-then-run leaks/desyncs; correctness needs the ThreadContextElement/PropagationContextElement model (re-apply on each resumption, 2159) — a per-poll obligation with no JVM analogue for value-based contexts.
- RAII Drop REPLACES try-with-resources Scope — and is strictly better for restore, but ONLY because restore is synchronous. Spring's AutoCloseable Scope guarantees the borrowed thread is left pristine via try-with-resources (2129); Rust gets this for free via Drop (cancellation can't skip it — no try-finally needed). The clash is asymmetric: this WIN holds for sync capture/restore, but does NOT extend to any async teardown (no async Drop on stable — nightly doc: tokio-shutdown crash), so a context concern needing async cleanup can't ride Drop.
- Send + 'static (and often Sync) bounds fracture 'capture any object'. Spring's ContextSnapshot captures any Object and moves it to any thread freely. A Rust snapshot/bundle that crosses a task hop on a multi-worker runtime requires every captured value be Send + 'static (R1) or Send + Sync + 'static (R2/R3). A !Send ambient value (a non-thread-safe request object) CANNOT be propagated at all — a hard compile-time wall where Spring has none. This makes 'which contexts are even propagatable' a type-level question absent from the JVM model.
- Type erasure without runtime reflection. Spring's accessors key by an Object key() and the registry is ServiceLoader-discovered at runtime (2124-2126). Rust has no runtime reflection: the registry must be SYNTHESIZED from compile/link-time contributions, values are erased to Box/Arc<dyn Any> keyed by a const ContextKey (Any+downcast, stable), and accessor discovery rides the same DCE-prone link-time substrate as every other contribution — a declared-but-unreferenced accessor crate silently contributes nothing (empty registry = silently-dropped context, a correctness bug with no error).
- Auto-discovery 'just works' magic is a DX hazard, not a feature, in Rust. Spring's ServiceLoader auto-discovery means 'merely having the jars on the classpath makes propagation just work — which can baffle anyone debugging why context moves' (2139). leaf has NO classpath; reproducing implicit cross-crate accessor discovery via linkme/inventory would import BOTH the silent-DCE failure mode (context silently NOT moving) AND the predictability hazard the #[global_registration] author warns against (a transitive dep silently injecting a context source). The rust-native answer leans toward SCOPED/explicit accessor opt-in + a startup self-check that lists active accessors — trading magic for the inspectability the charter §2.9 demands.
- Scope-based contexts (open/close a scope stack, with masking) don't map onto a value map. Spring's ObservationThreadLocalAccessor is scope-based not value-based: setValue opens a scope, no-arg setValue opens a NullObservation MASK rather than clearing (deliberately masking a leaked parent observation, 2147). A value-bundle model (R2/R3) represents values, not a scope stack with masking semantics — so observation/tracing-style scoped concerns need either an accessor that owns its scope-push/pop in capture/restore (R1) or a side mechanism; full parity with scope-masking is non-trivial.
- Opt-in-by-default for the RIGHT reason, but a different mechanism. Spring keeps propagation off (propagate-context=false) to avoid stale-tenant/security data bleed + per-task CPU cost (2155). leaf must ALSO default-off — but in Rust the data-bleed risk is even sharper (a reused async task slot / a wrongly-cloned bundle) AND the 'never inheritable' transaction case (2114-2118) becomes 'exclude this key from propagation by default', a per-key policy rather than Spring's per-holder InheritableThreadLocal=false field choice.

### Interactions
- **locale-context** — Tightest coupling; this feature's raison d'etre. locale-context DEFINES the holders / 'the current X' ambient lookups (current locale, request attributes, transaction sync) — the INPUTS this feature moves across boundaries. This feature provides the neutral capture/restore SPI (ContextAccessor + snapshot/bundle); locale-context's holders are the concrete sources that register accessors (or, in R2/R3, read from the framework task-local / explicit Context). The CRITICAL shared constraint: locale-context's holder storage mechanism MUST be task-scoped (or read the bundle), NOT a raw thread_local, or this feature cannot correctly propagate it across an .await. Where the value physically lives is locale-context's call; how it crosses a hop is this feature's.
- **task-execution** — Provides the wiring seam this feature plugs into. task-execution defines the TaskDecorator SPI + the ordered decorator chain (CompositeTaskDecorator analogue) and the executor that introduces the thread hops; this feature contributes the ContextPropagatingDecorator (R1) / supplies the with_context wrapper applied at submit (R2) that captures on the caller and restores/re-installs in the spawned task. Opt-in-by-default (spring.task.execution.propagate-context=false) is shared intent: task-execution exposes the per-executor/per-profile toggle, this feature implements what the toggle turns on. Hard ordering: the executor must exist before propagation can wire onto it.
- **event-multicaster** — Consumer via task-execution. Async event delivery routes listener invocations through task-execution's executor; without this feature's decorator, async listeners lose ambient context (Spring 1909: 'Async listeners lose ThreadLocal/MDC/Observation context unless the multicaster's TaskExecutor is decorated with ContextPropagatingTaskDecorator'). So enabling propagation on the multicaster's executor is exactly how an async @EventListener sees the publisher's request/locale/trace context — this feature defines that decorator/wrapper, the multicaster decides whether to apply it.
- **async-execution** — Consumer via task-execution. The #[async] method proxy hands work to task-execution's executor; ambient context (request/locale/tenant/trace) is lost across that hop unless this feature's propagation is enabled on the backing executor. async-execution is also the seam where R3's explicit-Context model struggles most (the proxy wraps user code and cannot thread a &Context param), forcing the ambient bridge — making this interaction a key Phase 2/3 judge of R1/R2-vs-R3.
- **transaction-management** — Provides the most delicate context AND the correctness boundary. The transaction/connection resource binding (TransactionSynchronizationManager analogue — thread-bound, NEVER inheritable, 2114-2118) is ambient context this feature governs, but with INVERTED default: a transactional connection must NOT silently propagate to a child task (it would shatter isolation and connection-pool accounting). So this feature must support per-key/per-concern EXCLUSION-from-propagation as a first-class policy ('never inheritable' realized as default-excluded), and transaction-management relies on that to keep its resource binding pinned to the originating unit of work.
- **scopes** — Provides the lifetime anchor for request/session/tenant context. The request/session scopes define the lifetime during which 'the current request context' is valid; this feature moves that scope's ambient value across the async task hops within that scope's lifetime. In R3, the explicit Context IS the scope-bound value resolved via the scope SPI. Cancellation/teardown of a scope must coordinate with this feature so a propagated context isn't read after its scope closed.
- **scoped-proxies** — Complementary mechanism for the same problem. scoped-proxies let a long-lived bean hold a stable proxy that resolves the live shorter-lived (request/session) target per call — an alternative to ambient propagation for crossing the longevity gap WITHIN a thread. This feature handles the orthogonal axis: moving the shorter-lived context ACROSS an async task hop. A scoped proxy resolving its target must read from the propagated context (this feature) when the call happens on a hopped task, so the two compose: proxy = which target, propagation = is the right ambient context present on this worker.
- **runtime-lifecycle** — Indirect, via the runtime-coupled task-local backing (R2/R3). The framework task-local storage that backs context-on-the-future is provided by the runtime integration and participates in the running-state machine; propagation behavior must be stable while the runtime is in its running phase. No direct lifecycle role for the SPI itself (it is stateless after refresh), but its storage backing shares task-execution's runtime-availability ordering constraint.
- **container-core** — Registers/selects the ContextRegistry and accessors through the engine + facade. The ContextRegistry (R1) is an infrastructure bean auto-detected and resolved like any other; accessors are contributions whose presence is surfaced by the facade's expected-vs-found self-check (the silent-DCE defense). Unlike task-execution's mandatory executor, a missing accessor is degraded-not-fatal (that concern just doesn't propagate), so the self-check is a WARNING/inspection surface, not a hard refresh failure — but it must still make the active accessor set legible to counter the 'baffling why context moves' hazard.
- **events** — Two-way: consumer and (potentially) source. Synchronous event dispatch preserves the caller's context naturally (same task); ASYNC dispatch (via event-multicaster + task-execution) needs this feature to carry context to the listener. Also, context-change could itself be observable, but the primary relationship is that this feature ensures an async-dispatched listener runs under the publisher's ambient context when propagation is enabled.
- **startup-instrumentation** — Diagnosability hook. The registered accessor set (R1) / the context bundle schema (R2/R3) and 'which executors/profiles have propagation enabled' are natural inspectable startup-diagnostic surfaces — directly countering Spring's 'baffling why context moves' hazard (2139) by making the propagation topology legible at boot (charter §2.9).
- **environment** — Source of the opt-in toggle. Whether propagation is enabled (per executor/profile), and which keys are excluded-by-default (transaction), are bound from the Environment — the rust-native realization of spring.task.execution.propagate-context and the per-concern propagation policy. Conditions over the Environment gate whether a given accessor/bridge wires up.
- **concurrency-contract** — Complements the safe-publication contract. concurrency-contract guarantees fully-built singletons are safely published and frames mutable-runtime-state safety as the developer's concern; this feature governs how PER-EXECUTION ambient state crosses task boundaries safely (immutable snapshots/bundles, restore-not-clear, Send/Sync bounds). The Send/Sync bounds this feature imposes on captured values are the rust-native teeth of 'what is safe to move across an execution boundary'.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- THE KEYSTONE (charter §3 explicitly deferred): what is leaf's rust-native answer to ThreadLocal holders across an .await? The candidates surfaced here — (a) a runtime registry of accessors over a task-scoped store with RAII restore (R1), (b) a poll-wrapping future combinator over one framework task-local re-installing on each poll, the ThreadContextElement/ScopedValue-analog (R2), (c) explicit Context-value threading with an ambient bridge only at seams (R3) — are the THREE shapes of the deferred 'async execution & context-propagation model'. This single decision determines whether locale-context's holders, task-execution's decorator chain, and this SPI are even implementable as designed. It MUST be co-decided with the holder mechanism (locale-context) and the executor model (task-execution), not in isolation.
- What task-local / scoped-context primitive does core define, and how does the runtime integration back its storage? std has no async-aware ScopedValue/task-local; tokio::task_local! is runtime-specific (violates §2.6). leaf likely must ship its own poll-wrapping task-local abstraction in core with runtime-provided storage — but is that the right primitive, or does leaf adopt a structured-concurrency scope model instead? Cross-cuts task-execution (runtime substrate), runtime-lifecycle, and the whole async model. Also: does the per-poll reinstall cost (R2) need a skip-when-unchanged optimization, and is that measurable as acceptable on hot paths (charter §2.4/§2.5)?
- How are Send/'static (and Sync) bounds reconciled with 'propagate any context'? A multi-worker runtime forces captured/bundled values to be Send + 'static (or Send + Sync + 'static); a !Send ambient value cannot cross a hop at all — Spring has no such wall. Does leaf mandate all propagatable context be Send+Sync+'static (losing some ambient values), or expose a single-worker/current-thread escape allowing ?Send context (and accept that swapping to multi-worker becomes compile-breaking)? Ties directly to task-execution's identical Send-bounds-vs-swap-by-config question and the RTN/trait_variant Send-variant nightly tensions.
- Is the propagated context ONE opaque bundle (R2/R3) or N independently-registered accessors (R1, Micrometer-faithful)? The bundle is cheaper and more inspectable but loses per-accessor restore-not-clear nuance and scope-based-accessor (ObservationThreadLocalAccessor open/close + NullObservation masking) parity; the accessor registry is faithful but pays a per-hop box-dance and reintroduces the silent-DCE empty-registry hazard. This is a shape call touching tracing/observation integration, WASM marshalling, and every consumer.
- How are scope-based contexts (tracing/observation: open a scope, mask with a Null scope rather than clear) represented when the model is value-based? Spring's scope-based accessor (2147) does NOT fit a value map. Does leaf require such concerns to own their scope push/pop inside an accessor's capture/restore (R1-style), or provide a separate scope-stack mechanism alongside the value bundle? Cross-cuts any future observability integration.
- Where does the explicit-vs-ambient line fall (the R3 question generalized)? AOP/interception seams (transaction, cache, retry, async-execution proxies), async-event dispatch, scheduling, and background-bootstrap all invoke user code with NO place to thread a &Context — forcing an ambient bridge even in an explicit-primary model. So even if leaf prefers explicit context (charter §2.3), it cannot avoid an ambient mechanism at those seams. The question: is ambient the primary model with explicit as an option (R1/R2), or explicit-primary with ambient only at seams (R3), and can the two coexist coherently without a desync failure mode? This binds to the AOP/interception substrate decisions.
- Accessor/bridge discovery: scoped opt-in vs auto-discovery, and the silent-DCE defense. Micrometer's ServiceLoader auto-discovery ('jars-on-classpath just works', 2139) maps onto leaf's DCE-prone link-time substrate AND triggers the #[global_registration]-author predictability warning. Does leaf require explicit opt-in of context sources (scoped, predictable, no silent-vanish) plus a startup self-check listing active accessors, or attempt auto-discovery? Binds to the deferred cross-crate composition model (§3); here a dropped accessor is a SILENT correctness bug (context stops moving, no error), so the self-check obligation is acute even though missing-accessor is degraded-not-fatal.
- What is the per-key propagation POLICY model, especially 'never inheritable' for transaction/connection resources (2114-2118)? Some context MUST propagate (locale, trace), some MUST NOT by default (transactional connection — propagating it shatters isolation), some is opt-in (tenant/security). Is this a per-key allow/deny list bound from the Environment, a typed marker on the context value, or per-concern accessor policy?
